**Previous (session 116, April 16, 2026):** Smoke-tested `brainchild pm` and discovered a flaky 5–15s shutdown hang on the tool-call path. Root-caused via stack dumps to a Playwright greenlet wedge on a dead CDP socket, landed two fixes, live-verified.

- **Smoke test found flaky teardown.** Three-trial matrix: A (quiet Ctrl+C after admission), B ("hey" → reply → Ctrl+C), C (Linear tool call → reply → Ctrl+C). A and B always clean (~1s). C wedged ~5–15s and the safety net caught the Playwright Node driver as an orphan. Not consistently reproducible — ~1 in 3 tool-call shutdowns.
- **Stack dump + instrumented `leave()` identified the wedge.** Added a `_browser_thread.join(timeout=5)` + `sys._current_frames()` stack dump to `connectors/macos_adapter.py:leave()`. Stack showed the greenlet parked in `sync_playwright/_context_manager.py:56 greenlet_main` → `run_until_complete(connection.run_as_sync())` → asyncio `base_events._run_once` → `selectors.KqueueSelector.select` → `kqueue.control(None, max_ev, timeout)`. `timeout=None` means "wait forever for I/O." The Node driver's CDP socket was dead (Chrome self-exits in `--headless=new` a moment after the Leave click) but the greenlet was waiting for CDP responses that never arrived.
- **First attempt (didn't fully fix):** removed the explicit `browser.close()` from `_browser_session`'s finally block. Rationale: `browser.close()` on a persistent context was the most obvious place for the hang. That helped the clean path but the same wedge signature reproduced inside `sync_playwright.__exit__` → `playwright.stop()` on the tool-call path — so the hang isn't unique to `browser.close()`, the whole context-manager exit can hit it.
- **Fix 1 — kill the Playwright driver directly.** New `_kill_playwright_drivers()` helper in `macos_adapter.py`: `pgrep -P <self_pid>` + `ps -o command=` to find children whose cmdline matches `playwright` + `run-driver`, SIGKILL them. `leave()` now does `_browser_thread.join(timeout=2)` → if still alive, call `_kill_playwright_drivers()` → re-join 2s. SIGKILLing the Node driver closes its socket, which unblocks the greenlet's `kqueue.select(None)`, the greenlet's event loop exits, and the context-manager unwinds cleanly. Shrinks the worst-case shutdown from 5–15s + outer safety-net (~7s total) down to ~3s deterministic, with no orphan.
- **Fix 2 — stop ChatRunner promptly on SIGINT.** The secondary symptom was a stray `ChatRunner: participant count changed 2 → 0` log appearing *after* `left meeting`. Root cause: the ChatRunner loop runs on the main thread, SIGINT runs the shutdown handler synchronously on the main thread (setting `_stop_event`, then blocking 6s inside `connector.leave()`), then returns control to the loop — which continues one more iteration's body before the top-of-while check. Added `if self._stop_event.is_set(): break` guards in `pipeline/chat_runner.py:_loop` after the blocking `read_chat()` and `get_participant_count()` calls, so the loop bails before logging/processing anything if stop was set while those were in flight.
- **Live-verified.** Three clean `brainchild pm` runs (quiet + two chat turns) — ~1s shutdown, no safety-net line, no stray logs. Then a tool-call run (`create an issue in linear to fold my laundry` → MOJ-11) deliberately hit the wedge: log reads `waiting for browser to close...` → `clicked Leave call` → `force-killed stuck Playwright driver pid=84330` → `left meeting` 4ms later. Total Ctrl+C → shutdown = 3.1s. No `Safety net: killing` line (inline SIGKILL beat the outer safety net). No stray `participant count changed` after `left meeting` (stop_event guard held). Fix working end-to-end on the exact scenario that was flaky.

**Open items:**
- **Smoke-test `brainchild engineer <url>` + `brainchild designer <url>`** under the positional CLI runtime architecture still deferred (was session 116's original agenda before the teardown hang took priority). Should be quick: startup logs for the right bundle's MCP servers / skill counts, a chat reply, at least one MCP tool call, and clean Ctrl+C.

**Previous (session 115, April 16, 2026):** Closed out Phase 15.5.3 by landing reliable auto-admit. Two iterations.

- **Iter 1 — added post-action verification + diagnostics.** Replaced the original "fire and log success unconditionally" admission block with: log the pill's actual `inner_text()`, log `admit_btn count=N visible=B`, save `debug/post_admit_pill_persisted.{png,html}` when the action runs but pill stays put, suppress the keyboard-fallback "admitted" log unless the pill disappears. Live test revealed the real issue: admission *did* succeed (participant count went 1→2 right after tray click), but Meet leaves the "Admit 1 guest" pill widget sticky in the DOM — visible to the human, visible to Playwright. So a "wait for pill gone" verifier loops forever.
- **Iter 2 — verification via participant-count delta + cooldown.** Swapped pill-disappearance check for `_do_get_participant_count(page)` polling for up to 3s post-click; success = count went up. Added a `(pill_text, participant_count)` cooldown so the same stale pill silently skips re-attempts until something actually changes. New diagnostic snapshot `debug/post_admit_success.{png,html}` saved on verified admission. Logs now read: `admit pill detected text='Admit 1 guest' count=1` → `admit_btn count=1 visible=True` → `admitted via tray click (verified — participant count 1 → 2)` then silence. Bonus: graceful shutdown also clean this run (Leave call clicked, browser closed in <1s, no 10s timeout).

**What just happened (session 114, April 16, 2026):** Live-validated Phase 15.5.3 in pieces, fixed three issues, added auto-admit plumbing (not yet confirmed).

- **Issue 1 fixed — "browser never opened":** On `brainchild pm` (no URL), `meet.new` was auto-joining us as the creator (we were already in the meeting). The pre-join flow raced for "Join now" / "Ask to join" / "Sign in" buttons and all three waits timed out → adapter treated it as `join_fail` and tore down. Fix: detect already-in state via `Leave call` button visibility *before* the pre-join race, skip camera toggle + join-button race, set `clicked_label = "already_in"`. Applied to both macOS and Linux adapters.
- **Issue 2 fixed — wrong meeting URL captured:** `wait_for_url(lambda u: ...)` was accepting Google's interstitial `https://meet.google.com/new?authuser=0&hs=178` as the "real" meeting URL because the old ends-with check didn't strip query strings. Bot then redirected to a real room (`ofz-btin-pcd`) and the human got handed the interstitial URL by `webbrowser.open`, which spun up a *different* fresh meeting under the user's account → bot and user in separate rooms. Fix: added `_is_real_meet_room(url)` using `urlparse().path` + regex `^/[a-z]{3,}-[a-z]{3,}-[a-z]{3,}/?

, passed as the predicate to `wait_for_url`.
- **Issue 3 fixed — no visible browser for the human:** Bot runs headless by design (`--headless=new` Chrome flag, invisible). That's correct. The missing piece was opening a *separate* visible tab for the human to join the same Meet. Fix: `__main__.py` now calls `webbrowser.open(meeting_url)` after the URL resolves (meet.new path only).
- **Host/knock problem — auto-admit plumbing added (not yet live-confirmed):** When the bot creates the meeting, the bot is host; the human knocks and needs to be admitted. Implemented auto-admit inside the adapter's in-meeting hold loop: every 2s, find the "Admit N guest(s)" pill via `get_by_text(regex)`, `.hover()` to trigger Playwright's real CDP mouse move (the pill is a *hover-tray widget*, not a button — synthetic `dispatchEvent` won't open the tray), then click the tray's `role=button name="Admit"`. Keyboard fallback: `pill.focus()` → `ArrowDown` → `Enter` (the pill's aria description says "Press Down Arrow to open the hover tray and Escape to close" — it's keyboard-activatable). Saves `debug/admit_diagnostic.{png,html}` on first hover-fire for future inspection. **Live test failed to admit** on last attempt; out of context before retry.
- **Doc scrub:** `./brainchild` → `brainchild` across 11 files (CLAUDE.md, roster READMEs, tests/15_5_*_testing.md, tests/11_*_testing.md, config.py error string) — the bash wrapper is symlinked into `~/.local/bin/` so bare `brainchild <name>` works from any directory.

**Open items:**
- **Auto-admit live-confirmation** — run `brainchild pm`, knock from another account, confirm admission fires. If it doesn't, inspect `debug/admit_diagnostic.{png,html}`.

**What just happened (session 112, April 16, 2026):** Walked `tests/15_5_2b_testing.md` T1–T7 against fresh Meet `cyv-utza-jxp`. The "soft" catalog restriction on Figma's official MCP turned out to be hard. Fell back to GLips mid-session, re-ran, all tests passed, then promoted GLips to bundle default with full doc update.

- **OAuth catalog gate is hard.** Official Figma MCP via `npx -y mcp-remote https://mcp.figma.com/mcp` failed at T1 with `HTTP 403: Invalid OAuth error response ... Raw body: Forbidden` raised from `mcp-remote`'s `registerClient` (dynamic client registration). Figma's `/register` endpoint rejects arbitrary clients — only those in Figma's MCP Catalog succeed. Brainchild is not (yet) in the catalog. Browser OAuth consent never opened because we didn't make it past `registerClient`. Pipeline correctly logged `MCP: 0/1 servers loaded (figma ✗)` and kept running.
- **Fell back to GLips** (`figma-developer-mcp`, PAT-authenticated). Env-mapped `${FIGMA_TOKEN}` → `FIGMA_API_KEY` for the child. Relaunched with `--force` (first-run left a stale session lock), bot joined, `MCP: 1/1 servers loaded (figma ✓)` with 2 tools (`get_figma_data`, `download_figma_images`).
- **All T1–T7 passed on the GLips path** (T4 marked N/A — GLips is read-only; verified by reading GLips' `src/mcp/index.ts`, which registers exactly two tools both with `readOnlyHint: true`, regardless of the PAT's write capability).
  - **T3 anti-hallucination guard live-demonstrated.** First test URL (`bTJlOWqmnmqVRmc2e4GGYd`, "Product carousel.") came back as a single RECTANGLE with an image fill — 592 chars, not a multi-card frame. Verified against Figma's REST API directly: the entire file contains just that one rectangle. Designer correctly read the thin payload and pushed back ("That's just a single image rectangle — no cards or spacing to review. Is this the right node?") instead of fabricating card critique. Iterated on a second URL (Plant-shop-curved-carousel from Community, node 1:2) which returned a 12KB payload; Designer produced a specific, grounded critique: "5 cards × 386×512px, 40px gap too tight, increase to 64–80px, plant-image breathing room, thumb-swipe targets."
  - **T5 first-fire over-reach (known fail).** Sonnet 4.5 loaded `design-review-feedback` on the casual "gut check — what's the first thing you'd change?" prompt and produced structured output. Per test plan this is the explicit fail signal. But the persona *can* do the conversational register: on redirect ("that was long, brief thoughts?") Designer replied with the canonical 1-sentence shape ("Bump the gap to 72px and make the plant names heavier — right now everything blurs together."). Trigger-sensitivity gap, not a capability gap. User chose to ship as-is and log the tuning note.
  - **T6 ✓ exactly as specified** — structured critique with `**What works**` / `**What breaks**` / `**Suggestions**` (Questions omitted per "empty sections omitted" rule), specific numbers, file URL appended, `max_tokens: 400` held.
  - **T7 ✓ graceful shutdown** — SIGINT → `MCP client shutdown complete` + browser close + `MacOSAdapter: left meeting`. Safety-net caught one orphaned `figma-developer-mcp` grandchild (npx spawns the real binary as a child; MCP client signals only the top-level process). `pgrep` clean after a couple seconds.
- **Grab `cursor-talk-to-figma-mcp` evaluated** mid-session (~25 mutation tools, no PAT — uses a Figma plugin + local WebSocket bridge via `bun socket`, `join_channel` tool to connect). Decided NOT to adopt as default: (a) plugin + bridge is more moving parts than the GLips npx-only default, (b) addressability regression — it operates only on the file currently open in the plugin, losing the "paste any Figma URL in chat" UX that's core to the hero moment. Documented as the canonical write-enabled power-up in `roster/designer/README.md` and `tests/15_5_2b_testing.md`'s Power-ups section.
- **Bundle flipped to GLips-as-default** — four files touched:
  - `roster/designer/config.yaml` — figma block: `npx -y figma-developer-mcp --stdio`, `env.FIGMA_API_KEY: "${FIGMA_TOKEN}"`, `read_tools: [get_figma_data, download_figma_images]`, pruned write-op hint, added anti-hallucination hint ("if get_figma_data returns a thin payload, say so plainly and ask for a different node-id — do not fabricate structure that isn't in the result").
  - `roster/designer/.env.example` — `FIGMA_TOKEN` required, comment points at `figma.com/settings`.
  - `roster/designer/README.md` — rewrote auth story, added "Which Figma MCP server?" section explaining default + Grab (write) + official-server (catalog-gated).
  - `tests/15_5_2b_testing.md` — intro flipped, Prep requires FIGMA_TOKEN, T1 expects silent PAT start + 2 tools, T3 expects `figma__get_figma_data` + anti-hallucination guard documented as an expected pass signal on thin fixtures, T4 N/A, Fallback → Power-ups with Grab and official-server configs. Prep step 6 now points at Plant-shop-curved-carousel from Community (the skincare fixture turned out to be the thin-rectangle file).

Security is Claude Code's problem (own permission model + worktree isolation). Loads user's `~/.claude/skills/`. Prerequisite: `claude` CLI installed. - **Key design decision: no shell MCP for engineer.** GitHub MCP covers code reading. Read-only shell is redundant (GitHub `get_file_contents` + `search_code` already do this). Full shell has real prompt-injection risk (arbitrary code execution as user). **Previous context (session 105, April 15, 2026):** Tiny Phase 11.7 fix + architectural discussion.

- **`config.py:79`** — changed `OPENAI_API_KEY = os.environ["OPENAI_API_KEY"]` to `.get(..., "")`. `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` was already using `.get()`.
- **`pipeline/providers/__init__.py` `build_provider()`** — added symmetric guard in the openai branch (`if not config.OPENAI_API_KEY: raise RuntimeError(...)`) matching the existing anthropic pattern. Each provider's key is now required only if that provider is configured.
- **Verified both paths:** `OPENAI_API_KEY= python -c "import config"` imports cleanly; building with `llm.provider: anthropic` + empty OPENAI_API_KEY works; forcing `llm.provider: openai` with empty key raises the expected clear RuntimeError. Unblocks Anthropic-only BYOK users and `--check-mcp` without a provider key.
- Committed as `d756962`.

**Architectural threads discussed (no code, deferred to post-MVP):**
- **Bash/code execution for Brainchild.** Options ranked: bash-MCP > skill-as-CLI-recipe > built-in. Bash-MCP gives per-tool confirm gating + audit trail (`READ_TOOLS`-style); skill-as-CLI-recipe is faster to author but every invocation looks like "bash ran" from `chat_runner.py`'s perspective. Noteworthy bash-MCP servers: `tumf/mcp-shell-server`, `blazickjp/shell-mcp-server`. Low adoption of bash-MCPs in general is because *sandboxing* (Docker/container per tool call) is the hard part, not the server.
- **Phase 15.5.1 is a roster entry WITH Claude Code delegation (revised session 107).** Originally (session 105) this was a gallery-only entry with no subprocess integration. Session 107 added a bundled `delegate_to_claude_code` mini MCP server (~50 lines Python) that runs `claude -p "<task>" --worktree` as a subprocess. This is NOT the heavy sub-agent architecture discussed in session 105 — it's a single tool call that shells out to the CLI. Security is Claude Code's responsibility (own permission model + worktree isolation). The engineer roster member both *resembles* Claude Code in shape (skills, engineering persona) and *delegates to* Claude Code for actual execution.
- **Modular sub-agent spawning (Codex / Claude Code / scrapers).** Recommended shape: model sub-agents as MCP tools exposing `spawn`, `status`, `result`, `cancel`. Default execution = async-detached. Deliver artifacts *around* Brainchild (sub-agent writes directly to Linear / GitHub PR / Slack), not *through* it (avoid blowing Brainchild's context window). Three design axes: transport (MCP-per-agent vs dispatcher vs subprocess), execution model (sync / async-blocking / async-detached), result channel (through Brainchild / around Brainchild). All post-MVP.
- **CLI-as-skill vs MCP.** CLI skills are great for breadth + fast authoring (SKILL.md + `--help`), but you lose structured tool-call logging, confirm gating, and `READ_TOOLS` allowlist. Recommendation: support both post-MVP; MCP stays for write-side tools where audit/confirm matters.
- **Claude API + shell vs Claude Code.** Same raw capability; difference is the curated loop (tool-call handling, context management, confirm UX, session state, hooks, subagents, skills, slash commands, IDE integration). Brainchild already has its own loop in `chat_runner.py` + `llm.py` — we are a Claude-Code-shaped thing, specialized for meetings.

**Next action:** Tackle **Phase 15.5.1** (`roster/engineer/`, ~2h — config.yaml + delegate_to_claude_code mini MCP server + README + skills + .env.example). After that: 15.5.2 (PM) → 15.5.2b (designer) → 15.5.3 (wizard) → 15.5.4 (meet.new) → 13 → 15.6 → 14 → 15 → 16. Phase 15.5.0 (rename) complete. MVP target still April 19, 2026.

**Previous context (session 104, April 14, 2026):** Walked `docs/11_4_testing.md` T1–T9 end-to-end against two fresh Meets (progressive mode → non-progressive mode → broken-config mode).

Available skills: hello, tone.` string. Error path works when forced.

- **T9** `SKILLS session summary: turns=1 load_skill_calls=1 by_name={'tone': 1}` emitted on Ctrl+C. Slash invocations correctly increment the counter.

**Previous context (session 103, April 14, 2026):** Implemented Phase 11.4 in one pass.

- **New `pipeline/skills.py`:** `Skill` dataclass + `load_skills(paths)`. Each config entry resolves to either a single skill folder (contains `SKILL.md`) or a parent dir scanned one level deep for `*/SKILL.md` — deeper nesting is ignored by design. Frontmatter parsed with `pyyaml`; malformed YAML, missing `name`/`description`, or unreadable files WARN + skip, never crash. `allowed-tools` parsed from either list or comma-string; anything outside the supported set (`load_skill` only for now) WARNs but the skill still loads (model may decline). Duplicate names across paths resolve last-wins + WARN. Startup banner matches the MCP shape: `SKILLS: N/M loaded (<name> ✓, ...)`.
- **`LLMClient.inject_skills(skills, progressive)`:** in progressive mode, system prompt gets a name+description menu plus instructions that restrict `load_skill` calls to requests that *clearly* match a description (prompt-tightening knob if the model over-calls). In non-progressive mode, full bodies are inlined. Also added an `extra_system` one-shot kwarg to `ask()` so slash-invocation can thread the skill body through without duplicating the user turn or mutating the persistent system prompt.
- **`ChatRunner` — three wiring additions.** (1) Accepts `skills` + `skills_progressive` kwargs and builds a name-indexed lookup. (2) `_tools_for_llm()` centralizes the MCP tools list and appends a synthetic `load_skill` function tool when progressive mode is on and at least one skill is loaded — replaced all three `self._mcp.get_openai_tools()` call-sites. (3) `_dispatch_result` short-circuits `load_skill` tool calls to a local handler (`_handle_load_skill`) that resolves the body and feeds it back via `send_tool_result` — auto-executed, no confirmation prompt. Slash-invocation (`/<name>` after the trigger strip) bypasses the round-trip entirely by passing the body via `extra_system` on a single `ask()` call. Unknown `/slash` is a pass-through (DEBUG log, no counter bump, no error).
- **SKILLS logging:** per-turn `SKILLS turn=N slash-invoke: <name>`, `SKILLS turn=N load_skill called: '<name>' (available: ...)`, `SKILLS turn=N unknown slash token: /<name>`, plus a session summary `SKILLS session summary: turns=N load_skill_calls=M by_name={...}` emitted from `stop()`. Per-turn visibility is the user's monitor for "is the model over-calling load_skill on chit-chat" — the open-item flag from session 102.
- **`config.yaml`/`config.py`:** `skills:` block with `progressive_disclosure: true` (default) and `paths: []`. Both flags surface as `SKILLS_PATHS` / `SKILLS_PROGRESSIVE_DISCLOSURE`.
- **`__main__.py`:** loader called up-front in both macOS and Linux paths, `inject_skills` lands *before* `inject_mcp_hints/status` so the final system-prompt ordering is base → skills → MCP hints → MCP status (most-dynamic last, future prompt-caching-friendly). `ChatRunner` gets `skills=` + `skills_progressive=` kwargs on both platforms.
- **`tests/test_skills.py` — 13 cases, all passing:** loader happy path, parent-dir scan, missing path (WARN + no crash), malformed YAML (skip + WARN), missing name/description (skip + WARN), duplicate last-wins + WARN, deep nesting ignored, `allowed-tools` WARN on unsupported entries, LLM menu-mode doesn't leak bodies, LLM full-body mode inlines them, `load_skill` tool gated on `progressive AND skills_loaded`, call-rate sanity (6 unrelated messages → 0 load_skill calls locally), slash-invocation increments counters + threads body into `extra_system`. Full existing suite (chat_hardening, 911/912/913, guardrails) still green.
- **Live-test plan at `docs/11_4_testing.md`:** 9 tests. T1 startup banner, T2 `load_skill` tool end-to-end (uses `skill-token-7h2x` sentinel string to prove body reached model), T3 slash fast path skipped the round-trip (verify zero `load_skill` tool_calls for that turn), T4 unknown slash pass-through, T5 over-eagerness regression (three unrelated messages → zero `load_skill` calls — this is the real behavioral test, since locally we can only check counter increments), T6 unknown skill name graceful error, T7 non-progressive full-body mode, T8 broken config degrades gracefully, T9 session summary on Ctrl+C.

**Design decisions made this session worth remembering:**
- **`extra_system` for slash invocation > pre-populating scratch.** The plan said "synthetic load_skill tool result pre-populated before the ask." Attempting that in `_scratch` would have conflicted with `ask()` clearing scratch at the start of every user turn. And prepending the body to the user message text would have both (a) required the meeting record to carry the expanded version or risk the LLM seeing two user turns, and (b) polluted the record on disk. A one-shot `extra_system` kwarg on `ask()` is invisible to the record, non-persistent on `_system_prompt`, and passes through to the provider as a normal system suffix. Cleanest fit for the constraint.
- **Unified `_tools_for_llm()` instead of ad-hoc list concatenation.** Three call-sites were doing `self._mcp.get_openai_tools() if self._mcp else None`. Moving that into one method that also knows whether to append `load_skill` means any future synthetic tool slots in without hunting for call-sites. Also lets the `load_skill` schema use an `enum` of loaded skill names to prevent the model from inventing one.
- **Auto-execute `load_skill` with no confirmation.** It's local, read-only, and purely a context-pull. Routing it through `_needs_confirmation` would have been the consistent path but would add friction for zero gain. The check in `_dispatch_result` lives at the top of the `tool_call` branch so it's hard to miss.
- **Log per-turn + session summary, not just summary.** The user's stated concern is "is the model calling load_skill too eagerly?" Per-turn logs let a human grep for occurrences in real time; the summary is the quick post-mortem. Without per-turn lines, a 20-turn meeting that ends with `load_skill_calls=3` doesn't tell you *which* turns fired.

**Known limitations remaining:**
- **Prompt-tightening is the real control if the model over-calls load_skill.** Code-side tests only verify our local counters don't fire on chit-chat; whether the LLM itself resists calling `load_skill` on "what's 2+2" is a behavioral property of the menu wording in `LLMClient.inject_skills`. T5 in the live-test plan is the only real check. If it fails, tighten the wording; do not add code gates.
- **`skills.local.yaml` personal overrides not yet implemented.** Deferred per session 102 — add post-MVP if users ask.
- **No hot reload.** SKILL.md changes require an Brainchild restart. Meeting-scoped sessions are short enough that this is fine.
- **Calendar-mode captions still need `ChatRunner.run_polling()`.** Carried from session 101.

**What just happened (session 101, April 14, 2026):** Walked the full captions live-test plan against `https://meet.google.com/fqx-xndc-odd` with a second human participant. Found and fixed three issues, then re-walked the critical subset (T1/T2/T6/T9) clean.

- **Issue #3 (CRITICAL — caused T6 to fail with 400 `messages: at least one message is required`).** `__main__.py` constructs `LLMClient` at line 201 *before* the captions path creates `meeting_record` at line 217, and only `ChatRunner` was ever wired to the new record (`chat_runner.py:66-72` only calls `llm.set_record(...)` when ChatRunner has to construct the record itself). With captions enabled, the LLM was holding its default empty in-memory `MeetingRecord` while everything else wrote to the on-disk one — `_tail_messages` returned `[]` and Anthropic rejected the call. **Fix:** added `llm.set_record(meeting_record)` immediately after `meeting_record = MeetingRecord(...)` in `__main__.py:218`. One line. Diagnosis was the longest part — the two startup log lines `MeetingRecord opened in-memory (no slug)` and `MeetingRecord opened …<slug>.jsonl` were the smoking gun once we knew to look.
- **Issue #1 (same-speaker dedupe).** Google Meet keeps the prior caption text visible in the same speaker's region, so each finalize re-emits everything Meet hasn't scrolled off yet. Without dedupe, a same-speaker continuation persists as "prior + new" instead of just "new." First attempt used strict `text.lower().startswith(prior.lower())` and that failed live because Meet auto-corrects casing/punctuation on prior text between finalizes (e.g. `"here,"` → `"Here."`). **Fix:** ported the `_normalize_for_match` token-prefix idea from `voice-preserved/pipeline/captions.py` into a new `_strip_prior_prefix(text, prior)` helper that compares words via `\w+` regex (case + punct insensitive) and cuts the original text at the end-position of the last matched token. Per-speaker dict so A's prior never affects B. Validated live across 5 finalize boundaries in a single Deepak monologue — every row contained only the new portion.
- **Issue #2 (cosmetic).** `caption_finalized` log line was truncating text at 80 chars (`text[:80]`), which made the log look out-of-sync with the JSONL. **Fix:** removed the slice. Pure cosmetic, no behavior change.

Added `tests/test_transcript_dedupe.py` — 7 cases (exact-prefix, case+punct drift, no-prefix passthrough, identical-text returns empty, empty-prior passthrough, end-to-end same-speaker dedupe via TranscriptFinalizer, per-speaker isolation). Full regression suite (11 test files) green.

**Design decisions made this session worth remembering:**
- **Look at voice-preserved before reinventing.** The voice branch's `pipeline/captions.py` already had a battle-tested fuzzy text-comparison helper for exactly the same Meet-rewrites-its-own-text problem (echo-suspect detection). Strict `startswith` failed live within minutes; the normalized token-prefix approach worked first try. When chat-mode caption code hits an edge case, voice mode probably hit it first.
- **Wire the LLM to the record at the construction site, not in ChatRunner.** ChatRunner's "if I created the record then I'll wire the LLM" pattern was a partial fix — it only covered the no-captions path. The real invariant is "whoever creates the record must tell the LLM about it." Adding the wiring directly under `meeting_record = MeetingRecord(...)` in `__main__.py` makes that invariant local and obvious. ChatRunner's branch can stay (it covers the case where ChatRunner is invoked without a pre-created record), but the captions path now has its own explicit wire.
- **Walking tests one at a time with the user is high-leverage.** The user typing "done" between tests + me grepping the log + reporting pass/fail/findings caught all three bugs in one ~30-minute session. T6 in particular only failed because we tested in order — by T7 we had a retroactive cross-check that proved the LLM behavior was correct and only the wiring was broken.

**Known limitations remaining:**
- **Calendar-mode captions still need `ChatRunner.run_polling()`.** `__main__.py:304` references `runner.run_polling(meeting_queue)` and `runner._in_meeting`, but neither exists on the chat-only `ChatRunner` — voice-era leftovers from before the decoupling. The late-bind fix (session 100) unblocked the *bridge* layer but the runner needs to be restored or replaced before captions actually flow through calendar mode. Out of scope for direct-URL caption use.
- **Dedupe doesn't handle Meet's roll-off perfectly.** If Meet rolls the caption pane such that prior is no longer at the start (only its tail overlaps the new text's head), `_strip_prior_prefix` returns text unchanged → some duplicate words emit. Would require a longest-overlap search instead of strict prefix; deferred unless real testing surfaces it.
- **No automated regression test for observer drift if Meet's caption DOM changes.** Same as session 99/100. T1 catches the acute case; a DOM-fixture replay would be better. Parked for Phase 12.

**What just happened (session 100, April 14, 2026):** Implemented the late-bind caption fix. `MacOSAdapter` now exposes `window.__onCaption` and injects the post-admission caption observer whenever `config.CAPTIONS_ENABLED` is true, regardless of whether `set_caption_callback` has been called yet — the Python-side bridge stub (`_on_caption_from_js`) drops captions silently when no callback is registered. `set_caption_callback(fn)` is now safe to call before OR after `join()`, and accepts `None` to unregister. Updated `__main__.py` to drop the misleading "calendar mode skipped" warning — the bridge will now be live, but per-meeting wiring still has to happen when a URL arrives via the calendar queue (and `ChatRunner.run_polling()` is missing from chat-only main; the `__main__.py:304` reference is a voice-era leftover that will need to be restored or replaced before calendar captions actually flow end-to-end). Added `tests/test_caption_late_bind.py` — 7 unit tests covering: drop-with-no-callback, register/receive, late-bind after first caption, swap routes to new sink, `None` unregisters, callback exception swallowed without breaking the bridge, `filter_caption` short-circuit. Full chat-only suite (9 files) still green. Committed as `1915473`.

**Design decisions made this session worth remembering:**
- **Late-bind over restructure.** Moving caption wiring into `ChatRunner.run()` would have dragged the connector lifecycle inward. Instead, expose the bridge once at browser startup and let the Python callback be swapped at any time. Smaller blast radius, parity-preserving for the direct-URL path, and naturally handles the calendar mode "browser up before URL arrives" sequencing.
- **Bridge stub is the gate, not the JS side.** The JS observer keeps firing `window.__onCaption(...)` whenever Meet renders a caption. The Python `_on_caption_from_js` is the cheap drop point when no callback is registered — keeps the JS observer free of gating logic and means swapping callbacks is just a Python attribute write.

**What just happened (session 99, April 14, 2026):** Ported the Google Meet caption pipeline from `voice-preserved` into main, parity-first on the battle-tested pieces. New `connectors/captions_js.py` holds the `CAPTION_OBSERVER_JS` verbatim (scoped MutationObserver on the Captions region, speaker-badge extraction, dedup, RAF batching) plus `enable_captions`, `captions_are_on`, and `filter_caption` helpers (icon-ligature + system-phrase rejection). `MacOSAdapter` gained `set_caption_callback(fn)`, a JS→Python bridge (`_on_caption_from_js`), `page.expose_function("__onCaption", …)` registered pre-navigation, and a post-join step that calls `enable_captions(page)` + injects the observer — all guarded on "callback was set," so chat-only runs don't pay for any of it. New `pipeline/transcript.py` owns finalization: `TranscriptFinalizer` buffers the latest (speaker, text, timestamp) and flushes on speaker-change OR silence-gap ≥ `CAPTION_SILENCE_SECONDS` (default 0.7s, configurable), appending finalized utterances to `MeetingRecord` as `kind: caption`. Only finalized text hits disk — no caption deltas. `config.yaml` gained a `transcript:` block with `captions_enabled: false` (privacy opt-in by default — captions pull in every participant's speech, bigger consent surface than chat-only). `config.py` exposes `CAPTIONS_ENABLED` + `CAPTION_SILENCE_SECONDS`. `__main__.py` (direct-URL macOS path) creates the `MeetingRecord` + `TranscriptFinalizer` *before* `connector.join()` so the callback is registered before `page.goto()`; the same record is threaded into `ChatRunner` via `meeting_record=` kwarg. `LLMClient._tail_messages` now includes `kind: caption` entries as `[spoken] <FirstName>: <text>` user-role messages, so tail naturally interleaves chat + captions by timestamp. System prompt updated with a one-line explanation that `[spoken]` lines are ambient context, not prompts to respond. Unit-tested the finalizer (speaker-change + silence-gap both flush; in-flight flushed on stop) and the interleaving (chat + caption rows in timestamp order with correct `kind` tags). All existing regression tests green (chat_hardening, 911_size_management, guardrails, mcp_client, anthropic_provider). Live test plan written at `docs/11_3_b_testing.md` — 9 essential-only tests from observer-attach through shutdown-flush.

**Design decisions made this session worth remembering:**
- **Port the observer JS verbatim; ignore the voice-loop 600-line tail.** Parity-first feedback is about preserving battle-tested code. The value in `voice-preserved/captions_adapter.py` is the `CAPTION_OBSERVER_JS` constant (lines 52-240) — scoped region selector, speaker badge logic, icon/system filtering, RAF batching. The rest was voice-coupling (wake detection, TTS echo guards, abort events, blocking `capture_next_wake_utterance()`) and a whole duplicate `MeetingConnector` subclass. Skipping that was correct; porting it would have been dead weight.
- **Unified single-stream transcript, tagged by `kind`.** Considered chat vs captions as separate streams and rejected: through the user lens ("what did Sarah just say about the deadline?", "summarize what we agreed"), the timeline reads naturally when speech and typed chat interleave in order. The LLM can distinguish via the `kind` tag + `[spoken]` prefix. Separate streams would be implementation hygiene at the cost of user-facing coherence.
- **Finalized utterances only on disk.** Deltas (streaming caption updates ~3/sec) stay in memory in the finalizer buffer; only the finalized utterance hits the JSONL. Keeps disk noise down, keeps `tail(n)` readable, matches the "one line per message" shape chat already uses.
- **Captions default off.** Chat is opt-in by nature (people type intending to address the bot). Captions ingest every participant's speech for the whole meeting. That's a meaningfully different consent surface, so the flag defaults `false`.
- **Wire captions in `__main__`, not `ChatRunner`.** `expose_function` must precede `page.goto()`. ChatRunner currently creates the `MeetingRecord` inside `run()`, which runs *after* `connector.join()`. Easier to create the record + finalizer in `__main__` (direct-URL path) and thread the record into `ChatRunner` via the existing `meeting_record=` kwarg than to refactor the lifecycle. Calendar-mode captions will need a separate pass (URL not known at startup).

**Known limitations to revisit post-live-test:**
- Calendar-polling mode skips captions (logged as a warning). When captions are enabled + no URL given at startup, `TranscriptFinalizer` creation is deferred — and never happens — because the URL arrives via the meeting queue inside `ChatRunner.run_polling`. Fix is straightforward: move the caption wiring down into `ChatRunner.run()` where the URL is known, but that means making `set_caption_callback` tolerant of being called post-`page.expose_function` registration (likely requires either re-exposing or always exposing when the connector supports captions). Not blocking MVP if the user's primary demo path is direct-URL.
- No automated regression test for observer drift if Meet's caption DOM changes. Live test T1 catches the acute case (observer didn't attach → no caption log lines → no JSONL entries). A stronger guard would be a DOM fixture saved from a real Meet caption region and replayed against the observer JS in a headless browser — worth adding in Phase 12 regression tooling if captions prove important to users.
- The in-flight drift on macOS DOM polling flagged in session 98 (bare `ok` confirmations occasionally dropped) may or may not intersect with caption-element observers. T1/T2 are the first signal check — if captions arrive cleanly through speech bursts, the polling-drop is isolated.

**What happened before that (session 97, April 14, 2026):** Positioning session. No code shipped (one new folder + README scaffolding). Competitive research surfaced [joinly](https://github.com/joinly-ai/joinly) as a near-peer: multi-platform (Meet/Zoom/Teams), BYOLLM (OpenAI/Anthropic/Ollama), MCP-shaped, voice + chat, MIT licensed, hosted cloud option, shipped 6+ months ago. Joinly's framing is platform/middleware-shaped ("expose meetings to agents") — their Reddit posts got meager response, plausibly because the pitch is abstract and they shipped the full surface at once.

Response: pick two implicit differentiators rather than feature-match. (1) **"Claude Code in your Google Meet"** as the launch hero framing — Phase 11.5 (skill import) is already on the roadmap and gives Brainchild a concrete, filmable hook that joinly can't easily copy without adopting Anthropic's skill format. Skills are provider-neutral (markdown + YAML frontmatter), so the framing works with OpenAI too; the "Claude Code" name is the marketing wrapper, not a fork. (2) **Opinionated quickstart** — "choose your fighter → add power-ups → go," delivered via an `agents/` gallery (ready-to-run folders committed to main, contributed via PRs) + a minimal `brainchild setup` wizard + README reading as Steps 1/2/3. Forks were considered as the community-proof primitive and explicitly rejected: galleries unify, forks fragment (Ollama library, LangChain templates, n8n templates, ComfyUI workflows, Vercel templates as reference patterns).

- **New folder: `agents/README.md`** — defines the gallery format (one folder per agent, each self-contained with `config.yaml` + optional `skills/` + `README.md` + `.env.example`), contribution rules (one job per agent; must run on a fresh clone; demo GIF of the artifact; no secrets), and usage instructions. `claude-code` listed as the canonical entry; slot left for a second chat-native agent (user will pick near launch from: standup / triage / incident-commander / interview-notes / research).
- **`docs/mvp-bar.md` updated** — positioning line adds the "AI power user's meeting bot / Claude Code skills natively / any markdown skill file with any model" framing. Three-part differentiation rewritten: #1 "Action, not access" now names joinly's category explicitly; #2 leads with Claude Code skill import as the sharpest implicit differentiator; #3 renamed to "Opinionated quickstart, not a framework" with the agents gallery + wizard as the delivery mechanism. Added a "3-step setup is obvious in under 30 seconds" entry to What Must Work. Added explicit non-goals for voice parity and Zoom/Teams parity with joinly — don't feature-match, fight on positioning. Added a full **Launch Strategy** section: hero framings by channel (Claude Code angle for r/ClaudeAI; standup bot for r/ExperiencedDevs; role-specific for niches), visual hooks (artifact-appearing-mid-sentence is the Pika-equivalent surprise moment; drag-drop-skills-folder as secondary), distribution levers ranked (direct SF outreach > newsletter/influencer mentions à la Pika > seeded `agents/` PRs > specific-JTBD Reddit posts; never generic "open source X" posts), and `agents/` as distribution primitive.
- **`docs/roadmap.md` updated** — new Phase 15.5 (Opinionated Quickstart) inserted between 15 and 16 with three steps: 15.5.1 `claude-code` starter agent (~1.5h), 15.5.2 minimal `brainchild setup` wizard (~2h), 15.5.3 second chat-native agent (~1h). Phase 16.1 README now explicitly requires 3-step structure and agents-gallery entry point. Phase 16.2 demo spec now calls out the mid-sentence-artifact visual hook. New Phase 16.3 Launch campaign prep (~3h) — draft three hero-framing posts, seeded PR plan, direct-outreach shortlist, newsletter mention targets. Post-MVP "Setup wizard" entry rephrased to clarify the minimal version ships in 15.5; full wizard (voice, MCP OAuth, polished UX) is post-MVP. New post-MVP "Agents gallery expansion" entry for ongoing recipe curation. MVP hour total bumped from ~40h to ~53.5h — right at the ceiling; 15.5.3 and 16.3 can slip post-launch if needed.

**Design decisions made this session worth remembering:**
- **Gallery pattern over forks.** Forks fragment git history and don't make the parent repo look alive. A `roster/` folder with PR contributions keeps everyone on main, makes contributors visible in the commit log, and turns every seeded-persona build into a permanent artifact pinned in the repo. This is the primitive; forks are not.
- **"Claude Code in your Google Meet" is framing, not product.** The product stays Brainchild; the campaign is CCiYM. Defaulting the skills path to `~/.claude/skills/` is a convenience for Claude Code users, not a lock-in — any markdown skill file works with any model.
- **CLI (end-user commands) vs. SDK (library for other devs).** Joinly's MCP server is effectively an SDK play. Brainchild's defensive lane is CLI-for-end-users — `brainchild setup`, future `brainchild skill add`, `brainchild doctor`, `brainchild check-mcp`. Don't race on SDK breadth.
- **Joinly is ahead on surface, not ready on positioning.** Don't chase voice, Zoom, or Teams pre-launch. Win on specificity and seeded community signal instead.

**What happened before that (session 90, April 12, 2026):** Shipped step 11.2 — Anthropic API backend. Went with a provider-neutral conversation shape (Option A) after user rejected a translator-shim approach that would have made Anthropic responses mimic OpenAI's object model ("I don't want our code to be more conducive/oriented toward one provider over another"). Partly redid session 89's work: replaced OpenAI-shaped response objects returned by `OpenAIProvider.complete()` with neutral `ProviderResponse(text, tool_calls: list[ToolCall], stop_reason)` dataclasses in `pipeline/providers/base.py`. History format is now neutral too: `{role: "user"|"assistant"|"tool_result", ...}` with `tool_calls: [ToolCall]` on assistant turns. `OpenAIProvider` and `AnthropicProvider` each translate neutral↔native at the boundary. `AnthropicProvider` (new file) wraps `anthropic.Anthropic`, translates tool schemas (OpenAI's `{function: {parameters}}` → Anthropic's `{name, input_schema}`), stop_reasons (`end_turn`/`stop_sequence`→`end`, `tool_use`→`tool_use`, `max_tokens`→`length`), assistant turns with tool_use blocks, and tool_result as user-role content blocks. Maps "prompt is too long" → `ContextOverflowError`. `build_provider()` factory in `pipeline/providers/__init__.py` reads `config.LLM_PROVIDER` and returns the right provider; raises if `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` is missing. All 4 call sites (`__main__.py` ×2, `pipeline/runner.py`, `cloud/docker/entrypoint.py`) now use `LLMClient(build_provider())`. Three surgical follow-ups after live testing exposed issues: (1) **parallel tool_use disabled** via `tool_choice={"type":"auto","disable_parallel_tool_use":True}` — Claude Sonnet 4.5 emits multiple tool_use blocks by default and our pipeline feeds one tool_result at a time; mirrors OpenAI's `parallel_tool_calls=False`. Logged as post-MVP item in roadmap. (2) **Prompt caching** on system + all tool schemas via `cache_control: {"type": "ephemeral"}` — unblocked 30k ITPM rate limit that killed follow-up turns when 72 tool schemas were resent every call. (3) **429 diagnostic** — `anthropic.RateLimitError` now logs a clear message with the ITPM cap, reset time, and tier-upgrade path. Also: `chat_system_prompt` in config.yaml now says "Render links as bare URLs, not markdown" (Claude was emitting giant `[label](url)` that flooded the chat panel). `anthropic` logger silenced to WARNING in both `__main__.py` and docker entrypoint (SDK dumps full request JSON at DEBUG — 20k+ tokens of tool schema per call). Unit tests: 11/11 pass in `tests/test_anthropic_provider.py` (new), plus existing test_911/test_913/test_guardrails updated to use neutral shape. Live-validated end-to-end in a chat-mode Meet with `provider: anthropic`, `model: claude-sonnet-4-5` across 4 user turns including a 4-tool fan-out ("can you check?" → 2× list_pull_requests + 2× list_commits across 2 repos) — no 429, concise replies, clean stdout. User will commit session 90's work.

**What happened before that (session 88, April 12, 2026):** Shipped step 10.6 — runtime failure backoff for MCP tool calls. `MCPClient` gained `_consecutive_errors: dict[str, int]`, `disabled_servers: dict[str, str]`, `record_tool_result(server, success) -> tripped_bool` (hardcoded `RUNTIME_FAILURE_THRESHOLD = 3`), and `server_for_tool(tool_name)` helper. `execute_tool` short-circuits any call whose server is in `disabled_servers` with the steering string: *"Server 'X' has been disabled for this session after repeated failures. This tool is unavailable. Do not retry; tell the user."* — the wording matters because that MCPToolError text becomes the tool-result the LLM sees back. `get_openai_tools` filters out tools whose server is disabled so the LLM stops attempting them. `LLMClient.inject_mcp_status` now takes a third `disabled_runtime` bucket and is idempotent: it tracks the last-injected text and replaces it on re-call, so a mid-session re-inject doesn't stack. Recording is centralized in `chat_runner._record_mcp_outcome(tool_name, success)` — called from the success path, the MCPToolError path, AND the timeout path (timeouts are enforced in chat_runner and never return through `execute_tool`, so they must be recorded here). On trip, chat_runner sends one announcement (*"The X server seems to be having issues — skipping it for the rest of this session."*) and re-injects MCP status with the merged `failed_to_load | disabled_runtime` state. Unit-tested in `tests/test_mcp_client.py` (new Test 6 covers below-threshold, reset-on-success, trip at N, no-re-trip, tool filtering, and short-circuit steering text). Live-validated in a chat-mode Meet using `debug/flaky_mcp_server.py` (exposes a single always-failing `check_weather` tool): three weather questions produced `failure 1/3 → 2/3 → disabled`, single chat announcement fired, `tools=73 → 72`, fourth weather question produced the steering reply without a tool call, Linear/GitHub unaffected. Committed as `feat: step 10.6 — runtime failure backoff for MCP tool calls` (2b3343a). Session 86's voice-path alone-exit was confirmed live-working by user.

Banner: after discussing liabilities of not running `--check-mcp` before launch (30s startup delay from a hung server, silent auth failures, first-time DIY users missing log-only signals), added `_print_mcp_startup_banner()` in `__main__.py` that prints a one-line MCP status to stderr right before browser join, wired into both chat-mode launch paths. Non-blocking — failures warn but don't abort. Output examples: `MCP: 2/2 servers loaded (linear ✓, github ✓)` on success; `MCP: 2/3 servers loaded (linear ✓, github ✓, weather ✗) — run --check-mcp for details` on partial failure. Verified against a patched config with a broken weather server. Committed as `feat: MCP startup banner for broken server visibility` (4fac579). User added Phase 11.4 (skill file loading — markdown files in `skills/` appended to system prompt) as the MVP customization layer; committed as `docs: add Phase 11.4 — skill file loading` (5ad7143). 10.3 detail below:

Shipped step 10.3 — user-defined MCP server scaffolding, with live end-to-end validation. Also closed two stale open concerns (session-82 correction re-propose flow confirmed validated during 10.2 live test; Linear-vs-GitHub routing bias addressed by a new chat system-prompt line clarifying "repo" = GitHub). Deleted three orphan test branches (`test/pr-fixture`, `test/pressure-test`, `test/pressure-test-clean`) local + remote where present. 10.3 implementation is four focused changes: (1) `config.py:_resolve_env_vars` warns "MCP USER CONFIG: server 'X' env var Y is empty or missing from .env" at config-load when `${VAR}` resolves to empty; (2) `pipeline/mcp_client.py:_classify_startup_failure` unwraps anyio `BaseExceptionGroup` and produces plain-English reasons for missing-binary (`FileNotFoundError`), startup timeout (`TimeoutError`), and binary-exits-before-handshake (matches "process exited"/"broken pipe"/"eof"/"connection closed" substrings). `MCPClient.failed_servers: dict[str, str]` records per-server failure reasons for downstream consumers; (3) `pipeline/llm.py:inject_mcp_status(loaded, failed)` appends loaded/failed server lists to the system prompt so the LLM answers accurately when asked about failed servers. Wired in both `__main__.py` chat paths alongside existing `inject_mcp_hints` / `inject_github_user`; (4) `python __main__.py --check-mcp` loads config, starts every configured server, prints `✓ name (N tools)` / `✗ name <reason>`, exits 0 if all loaded else 1. Validation: patched `config.yaml` with a `weather` server pointing at a nonexistent binary, joined a live Meet in chat mode — LLM declined generic "what's the weather" gracefully, answered "which servers failed to load?" with "The weather server failed to load. Please check /tmp/brainchild.log for details.", and Linear tool calls worked normally. `config.yaml` reverted after test. Committed as `feat: step 10.3 — user-defined MCP server scaffolding`.

**What happened before that (session 86, April 12, 2026):** Tangent session — meeting-exit logic. User asked what conditions cause Brainchild to self-terminate and identified a missing MVP case: if Brainchild has seen other participants and they all leave, Brainchild should drop. Audit confirmed only one auto-leave heuristic existed (past end-time + user display name absent, in CaptionsAdapter); chat path had no self-termination at all. Implemented alone-exit auto-leave: (1) new `agent.alone_exit_grace_seconds` config (60s default); (2) ChatRunner tracks `saw_others` + `alone_since` in its polling loop — after count>1 observed, drop to count==1 starts grace timer; on timeout, logs, prints user-facing message, calls `connector.leave()`, returns; (3) CaptionsAdapter gets parity logic alongside the existing end-time check, sharing the 30s `last_presence_check` throttle, pulled out of the end-time conditional so both can run independently. Pre-join/waiting-room false positives ruled out three ways: both loops only run post-admission, `[data-requested-participant-id]` is a meeting-only DOM, and the `saw_others` latch can't flip until count>1. Tested live in chat mode: saw 0→2 flip, 2→1 start timer, 60s later clean auto-leave with Leave-call click + browser close + MCP shutdown. Voice path untested per user direction. Committed as `feat: auto-leave when Brainchild is alone after others were present (session 86)`.

**What happened before that (session 81, April 12, 2026):**

Session 81: Reliability fix outside the phase plan — camera-toggle failure on macOS pre-join. User reported camera stayed ON in a live session; logs showed the existing "could not confirm off state" warning fired, but code only logged and proceeded. Diagnosis: the click at `macos_adapter.py:528` returned success (5s `wait_for` passed), but the 3s post-click `data-is-muted="true"` wait timed out. Debug HTML confirmed the button existed with `data-is-muted="false"` — click didn't toggle state. Two root-cause candidates indistinguishable from existing logs: hydration race (button in DOM but listener not wired) vs. overlay intercept. Restructured the pre-join flow: (1) removed camera selectors from the step-2 DOM-ready wait (they race with join buttons at different times); (2) added a dedicated camera step after state gates that waits for the button with `data-is-muted` attribute present (hydration signal); (3) added `_probe_camera_button()` diagnostic logged pre-click and on failure — captures `hydrated`, `data_is_muted`, rect, `elementFromPoint` result, `intercepted` flag; (4) on confirmation failure, falls back to `⌘+E` keyboard shortcut (bypasses both overlay and hydration by going through Meet's global hotkey handler); (5) if both fail, sets `self._camera_on_at_join = True` for downstream visibility. `macos_adapter.py` only — Linux/Docker/Captions adapters untouched per surgical-change preference. Not validated live yet.

**Also this session (session 82, April 12, 2026):** Live pressure-tested BYOMCP guard rails and confirmation handler. Guard rails validated: `.mp3` pre-execution block fired correctly. Three LLM behavior issues surfaced: (1) LLM adds `state='unstarted'` to `list_issues` despite "all open" — root cause was our hint listing state types without marking them optional, and the Linear MCP schema offering the field with no default guidance. Fixed: made hint conditional ("When the user specifies a state...") and added "omitting it returns all states." Multi-state filtering (e.g. "incomplete" = unstarted + started) is an MCP limitation — single `state` param only. (2) LLM guessed `repo='our'` literally instead of asking which repo. Fixed: added system prompt directive "ask the user to clarify rather than guessing" for ambiguous required params. (3) Confirmation rejection said "OK, cancelled" and dropped the interaction — LLM never re-proposed. Fixed: correction handler now passes `tools=` to `send_tool_result` (so LLM can re-issue tool calls) and dispatches the response (text → chat, tool_call → re-confirmation). Also discovered the correction response was being swallowed by `_collapse_tool_exchange` — the LLM generated a clarifying question but it was never sent to chat because the return value was discarded. (4) "read logo.png from the repo" routed to `linear__list_projects` — conversation context bias from prior Linear-heavy usage primed the model away from GitHub tools. No code fix; system prompt clarify-don't-guess directive may help.

**Audit walk-through complete (session 92, April 13, 2026):** All 10 layers of `docs/oss-audit-report.md` parsed collaboratively with user and actioned in `roadmap.md`. Every layer was stripped from the report and replaced with a pointer note explaining where its findings landed. Key outcomes:

- **Promoted pre-MVP to Phase 11:** 11.6 conversation history persistence (L6-a, ~1.5h — JSONL on disk, not the full `ConversationStore` protocol); 11.7 provider API keys optional at import (L1-c, ~15m — real BYOK-Anthropic crash fix).
- **Fast-follow bucket (pre-MVP if time permits, ~10h 45m total):** configurable log destination + level + redaction (absorbs L1-b + L9-b + L10-b); `ChatSource` seam + stdin source (absorbs L1-a + L2 + L3-c, bumped to ~6h to include pushing Meet-specific concerns into `MeetAdapter` and promoting `leave_when_alone` to a config toggle); per-server quirk config (L3-b + L9-a partial — `strip_args`, `identity_tool`, overridable `prompts.identity_guidance`); open provider registry (L4-b — dict + `register_provider`); framework-owned strings as config templates (L3-d + L9-a partial — absorbs `inject_mcp_status` as a global `prompts.mcp_server_unavailable` template).
- **Post-MVP firm:** Skill manifest + neutral `ToolSchema` + install consent (~10-14h, bundles L3-a + L4-a + L5-a + L5-b).
- **Dropped entirely:** L6-b (retention-policy abstraction — current dial + auto-collapse already matches intended design); L7 (daemon/API split — reviewed against hosted-bot vision, containerizing the monolith is the right path, daemon/API is YAGNI); L8-a (CLI flag overrides — field norm for config-heavy long-lived tools like kubectl/terraform/docker-compose is YAML-first).
- **New Post-MVP phase added: Hosted Brainchild** (~30-35h) — containerize the monolith, per-meeting ephemeral containers, invite-receiver (email or Calendar webhook), orchestrator, hosted Google auth, multi-tenant config isolation, observability. North star vision: Shopify-style inviteable bot.
- **Compliance affirmed:** L10-a — repo-wide grep verified zero outbound network activity beyond configured LLM provider, configured TTS, and opted-in MCP servers. Zero-telemetry commitment holds.

**Framing reframes that happened during the walk-through (worth remembering):** (a) The product IS a meeting bot — needing a meeting URL isn't a violation; the violation was `ChatRunner` being welded to the Meet connector. (b) The ethos doc's "layered YAML → env → CLI → per-skill" was one-size-fits-all; meeting bots aren't CLI tools, and YAML-first with no CLI flags is the correct shape for config-heavy long-lived agents. (c) Daemon/API/client separation is for tools where state outlives client sessions or multiple clients hit one instance simultaneously — neither applies to Brainchild. (d) The skill-manifest/install-consent commitment is a mature-product concern, not a day-0 demo concern, and deferring it is honest.

Without guidance, the first meeting launch would trigger an OAuth popup mid-join.
