**Architecture note (session 47):** CaptionsAdapter and MacOSAdapter have duplicated browser session logic (~150 lines each). User considered refactoring into a shared base but decided against it — chat is shipping first, so keeping them separate avoids unnecessary abstraction. Revisit when both paths need parallel maintenance.

**Architecture note (session 51):** MCP integration uses a dedicated asyncio event loop thread to bridge the async MCP SDK into our sync codebase. Each MCP server runs as a long-lived `_ServerHandle` async task — required because `stdio_client` uses anyio task groups that must stay in one task. Tool names are namespaced as `server__tool` (e.g., `linear__create_issue`) to avoid collisions across servers. Confirmation flow: LLM returns tool_call → Brainchild asks user in chat → user confirms → tool executes → result fed back to LLM → summary sent. `LLMClient.ask(tools=None)` returns a plain string (voice path unchanged); `ask(tools=[...])` returns a structured dict.

**Architecture note (session 54):** Chat message detection now uses a two-layer approach: MutationObserver in the browser for instant detection, with 0.5s Python polling as a fallback drain cadence. The observer seeds `__brainchildSeenIds` with existing messages on install to avoid replaying history. Participant count uses `[data-requested-participant-id]` which reliably tracks actual in-call participants (not invited-but-absent). The count is 2× `rosterCount` due to UI duplicate elements, so we use `requestedParticipants` instead.

---

## Hard-Won Knowledge (read before touching relevant code)

- **User-scoped filesystem state belongs under `~/.brainchild/`, never at the repo root via `_BASE`/`_ROOT` walk-ups** (session 158). Four artifacts — `browser_profile/`, `auth_state.json`, `.env`, `debug/` — were pinned at the repo root via `os.path.dirname(... __file__ ...)` chains or `Path(__file__).parents[3]`. Works in dev mode; in an installed package (`uv tool install`, `pip install`) `__file__` lives in `site-packages/` and the walk-up resolves into a non-writable location (or worse — `site-packages/debug/`, which some shared tooling might actually touch). Two distinct failure modes result. Mode A — install broken. User runs the installed CLI, the wizard tries to create `site-packages/.env`, `open("a")` raises PermissionError, or silently writes to a location that later gets clobbered by a package upgrade. Mode B (insidious) — latent divergence even in dev mode. `setup.py` wrote `.env` to `<repo-root>/.env` while `__main__._bootstrap_claude_imports` and `brainchild edit env` targeted `~/.brainchild/.env`; users' API keys landed in the wrong file on any code path that took the home-anchored read. No test caught it because tests checked "did config parse?" not "does the file the wizard writes equal the file config reads?" — a whole class of bug between two parts of the codebase that happen to agree on a hardcoded literal. The patterns that produce the bug, each ugly in its own way: `os.path.dirname(os.path.dirname(... __file__ ...))` walk-ups ≥3 levels (trying to find the "repo root" — doesn't exist in site-packages); relative-path literals (`"./foo"`, `"bar.json"`) assigned to `*_DIR`/`*_FILE`/`*_PATH` constants (resolves against CWD when a function that touches the path runs); `os.path.join(os.path.dirname(__file__), "..", ...)` in scripts ascending out of the package. Legitimate `__file__` uses: within-package bundled resource lookup (`Path(__file__).parent / "agents"` from inside `src/brainchild/`) — that's pinning at the *package* root, not the *repo* root; still works under site-packages. The fix protocol when you find a broken one: (1) make the config constant absolute via `str(Path.home() / ".brainchild" / "...")`; (2) in call sites, use `config.X` directly (no more walk-up dance); (3) if it's user data that exists on deployed machines today, add a one-shot migration shim to `__main__.py._migrate_legacy_user_artifacts` that `shutil.move`s the legacy location into the new one on next startup (target-exists branch protects live data from being clobbered by stale legacy); (4) update `.gitignore`, `README.md`, `CLAUDE.md` for the new canonical location; (5) add a regression guard in `tests/test_path_resolution.py` — Layer 1 (all `*_DIR`/`*_FILE`/`*_PATH` attrs absolute + under HOME) and Layer 2 (wizard-write-path equals runtime-read-path byte-exact) both have anti-drift coverage now; new path constants must be added to the allow-list or the test fails. If you're ever tempted to write `os.path.dirname(os.path.dirname(... __file__ ...))`, stop — you probably want `Path.home() / ".brainchild"` or `Path(__file__).parent / "<bundled-resource>"` depending on whether it's user data or package data.

- **Two uncoordinated stopwatches with the tighter one winning — fingerprint: `Tool 'X' failed: ` with nothing after the colon** (session 157). Live-QA reported a Claude Code delegation "failing" while the delegated work actually completed seconds later. Log showed tool started 21:34:46.470, failed 21:35:16.475 — exactly 30.0s — with an empty error string after "failed:". The bot's outer heartbeat loop in `chat_runner._execute_and_respond` correctly read the user's `tool_timeout_seconds: 600` override, but `_ServerHandle.call_tool` in `pipeline/mcp_client.py` had a separate `future.result(timeout=30)` that nobody told about the override. Two ceilings, uncoordinated; the inner one fired first. Root cause worth remembering beyond this specific code: `concurrent.futures.TimeoutError` stringifies to `""`, so `f"Tool 'X' failed: {e}"` produces a signature empty-tail error line that's very distinctive in logs — if you see that exact shape, look for a `future.result(timeout=...)` call somewhere downstream of the thing that hit the deadline, not at the deadline you configured. The asyncio task kept running after the inner timeout, so the subprocess finished, files landed, and the user saw the "failure" *plus* completed work — which is a separate telltale (the bot apologizing for something that visibly worked = the call path timed out but didn't actually cancel). Fix approach: collapse to one source of truth. Don't add a "safety margin" between two timeouts; pick one layer to own it. Here, MCP layer owns it via a resolved per-server value; chat_runner just drives heartbeats. If you ever find two timeouts living in the same code path, one of them is wrong — either redundant or actively undercutting the other.
- **The setup wizard's step 4 was silently wiping `personality` and `ground_rules` on empty input** (session 155). `_step4_system_prompt` did `state.bot_cfg["personality"] = new_text; state.bot_cfg["ground_rules"] = ""` unconditionally, where `new_text` is the user's keystrokes from the inline prompt. Hit ENTER with no input → `personality = ""` and `ground_rules = ""`. The hint copy ("Leave empty to skip") matched the buggy behavior so it didn't read as a bug; the comment near the `_new_agent` baseline (lines 303–304) said "Personality + ground_rules carry pm's defaults through — steps 4/5 offer approve-or-start-blank so users can inherit or replace" which described the intended UX, not the actual code. Symptom on the user's end was much worse than "bot has no personality" — the model loses the "1–3 sentences" cap from ground_rules and starts writing essay-length replies in chat. Diagnosis was straightforward once we suspected the system prompt: print-composed `SYSTEM_PROMPT` length was tiny vs the bundled config's 2.6KB. Fix: branch on `if new_text:` — only assign when non-empty, otherwise leave `state.bot_cfg["personality"]` / `state.bot_cfg["ground_rules"]` alone so the preset's defaults flow through. Hint copy updated to "Leave empty to keep the preset's defaults" so the language matches the behavior. No tests existed on `_step4_system_prompt` before this — none added either, since the wizard suite uses interactive Prompt.ask which is hard to fixture.
- **Google Meet's chat panel hides messages received before you opened it; bot intros need to wait for a human** (session 155). The bug surfaced as "`brainchild run claude` (no URL) doesn't post an intro." Logs disagreed — `MacOSAdapter: chat sent: "I'm Claude Code…"` lines were always present, ~3s after bot join in both meet.new and URL paths. Real diagnosis: in meet.new mode, the bot joins instantly via headless Chrome and the launcher fires `webbrowser.open(url)` to pop the user's default browser; the user then has to traverse Meet's pre-join screen (mic/cam settings → "Join now") and click the chat icon to open the chat panel. Total elapsed: 5–15s. The bot posts its intro at T+3s. Meet does NOT replay messages posted before the chat panel was opened, so the user sees an empty chat and assumes the bot ghosted. URL-given mode worked because the user was usually already in the meeting (chat panel open) when they ran the CLI. Fix: gate the intro-post in `chat_runner._loop` on `saw_others` (at least one other participant has been detected in `get_participant_count()` checks). Bot waits silently until a human joins, then posts. URL-with-humans-already-there path is unchanged because `saw_others` flips on the first 3-second participant check. Edge case: bot alone forever → never posts intro (auto-leave grace timer handles cleanup). The "tradeoff" framing is a phantom — no human ever experiences a behavior change except the fix. Same general lesson elsewhere: any fire-and-forget chat send shortly after join needs to wait for a verified audience.
- **`rich.live.Live` + `Prompt.ask` don't compose; reach for `readchar` and a callable right-pane instead** (session 120). Building the picker primitive surfaced the architectural fork: Rich's `Prompt.ask` writes to the console synchronously and Live owns its render region, so they fight over the cursor + cause flicker if you try to host text input inside a Live block. The clean split is: picker phases own the screen via Live and read raw keys via `readchar.readkey()` (returns `\x1b[A` for arrows, `\n`/`\r` for enter, ` ` for space — handle both `\n` and `\r` for cross-platform Enter). Text-input phases (custom-mode name prompts, API-key prompts) drop the Live region entirely and use `Prompt.ask` normally. Trying to keep the build card "always visible" through text-input phases is a maze for very little gain — the picker phases are where the live vibe pays off; text input is short and sequential. Second design lever: the picker's right pane needs to support both per-choice previews (step 1 portrait gallery — preview is a property of the highlighted choice) and global state previews (steps 2/3 build card — preview reflects toggled state across the whole list, doesn't depend on cursor). One-knob solution: a `right_pane: Callable[[cursor, checked], Renderable]` argument that wins over per-choice `Choice.preview` when provided. The wizard passes `right_pane = lambda c, ch: state.card(mcps=names_where(ch))` — closes over global wizard state and re-renders on every keystroke without mutating state during render.
- **Rich markup parser swallows `[x]` silently — use non-ASCII glyph in brackets** (session 119). Rendering a checked-state marker in toggle lists with `[x]` made it render as a blank because Rich treats `[x]` as a (non-existent) style tag and strips it. The asymmetry only showed up when some items were default-checked; `[ ]` (with a space) printed literally because " " isn't a valid style name. Fix: switch to `[✓]` — non-ASCII content inside brackets isn't parsed as a style. Same applies to any character that *could* be a style name (`[u]`, `[i]`, `[b]`, `[red]`, etc). Reach for a glyph the parser won't try to interpret, or escape with `\\[` if you really need ASCII brackets.
- **`MeetingRecord.tail()` must scope to the current session or the LLM echoes prior runs' replies and stops calling tools** (session 117). `MeetingRecord` is append-only JSONL keyed by meet slug — same URL ⇒ same slug ⇒ same file. When a user reruns `brainchild <name> <url>` against the same meeting (common during development), the file accumulates every prior session's entries. `tail(n)` was originally implemented as "last n lines of the file regardless of origin," which meant `LLMClient._tail_messages()` replayed the agent's own prior assistant replies back to it as `role="assistant"` history. Downstream effect: the model pattern-matched on its prior outputs and replied directly instead of calling the MCP tool that originally produced those outputs. Worst case observed in diagnosis: user said "mojo jojo" → bot replied `Created https://linear.app/mojo-jojo/issue/MOJ-11/fold-my-laundry` with **zero tool calls logged** — it hallucinated the URL from MOJ-N patterns in prior replies. The tell is extremely easy to miss: fresh-slug runs (`brainchild <name>` with no URL, which hits meet.new and gets a fresh slug) work fine; only same-URL reruns regress. Symptom from the logs is `len(messages)=20/22/...` on the problematic runs vs `len(messages)=1` on the fresh-slug run. Fix: write a `{"kind": "session_start", "timestamp": ...}` boundary marker on every `MeetingRecord.__init__`; `tail()` scans back from the end of the parsed entries to the most recent marker and returns only entries after it. Raw JSONL preserves the full audit (you'll see two `"session_start"` lines in the file after a rejoin). Don't "fix" this by purging old history — the file is valuable as a durable record of the meeting; only the *LLM-visible window* needs to be session-scoped. Tests in `tests/test_chat_hardening.py::test_meeting_record_tail_roundtrip` cover the reopen-yields-empty-tail contract.
- **Startup banners must print before log output or they get buried; don't wait for MCP status if the loadout names are enough** (session 117). First attempt at the 15.5.4 startup banner called `_print_startup_banner(mcp, skills)` *after* `mcp_thread.join()` so the loadout line could show per-server ✓/✗ status. Live-verified on `brainchild pm`: the banner printed correctly but sat 40+ lines down in scrollback, below MCP tool-discovery chatter + `TIMING` lines + `meet.new resolved to ...` → user's first reaction was "where's the banner?" Even though the banner has blank lines above/below it, in a log stream it reads as just another log entry. Fix: print the banner as a *boot splash* — fire it immediately after `load_skills(config.SKILLS_PATHS)`, before any MCP connect or browser launch. Drop the ✓/✗ from the loadout line (the existing per-server MCP connect logs already surface status; startup failures are obvious from behavior). Show names only: `linear · github · 4 skills · claude-sonnet-4-5`. Rule of thumb: if a user-facing splash depends on info that takes measurable time to fetch, either print it twice (splash early + status line later) or drop the fetch-dependent part.
- **Playwright `sync_playwright.__exit__` can wedge forever on a dead CDP socket; removing `browser.close()` isn't sufficient; SIGKILL the Node driver to unblock it** (session 116). With `launch_persistent_context(headless=False, args=[..., "--headless=new"])`, Chrome sometimes self-exits a beat after the Leave-call click — the CDP socket dies but Playwright doesn't notice. Any subsequent teardown that sends a CDP request (explicit `browser.close()`, OR the context-manager exit's `playwright.stop()`) waits for a response that never arrives. Stack signature to recognize: `greenlet_main` → `_loop.run_until_complete(connection.run_as_sync())` → asyncio `_run_once` → `KqueueSelector.select` → `kqueue.control(None, ...)` with `timeout=None` (no scheduled work, waiting on I/O forever). Rough guide to reproducibility: flaky — roughly 1 in 3 tool-call-path shutdowns hit it, clean-path shutdowns almost never do. First instinct was "remove `browser.close()` since `sync_playwright.__exit__` handles teardown" — that helps the clean path but the same wedge signature reproduces inside `__exit__` on the tool-call path. The fix that actually works: force-kill the Playwright Node driver child process directly — that closes its socket, which unblocks the greenlet's `kqueue.select(None)`, which lets the asyncio loop exit, which lets the context-manager unwind. Implementation in `connectors/macos_adapter.py`: `leave()` does `_browser_thread.join(timeout=2)` → if still alive, `_kill_playwright_drivers()` (pgrep `-P <pid>` + match cmdline on `playwright` + `run-driver` + SIGKILL) → re-join 2s. Don't try to rely on Playwright's graceful teardown path when the CDP socket might be dead — just kill the driver.
- **ChatRunner's main-thread loop needs `_stop_event` guards after any blocking call to avoid a stray post-shutdown iteration** (session 116). `ChatRunner._loop()` runs on the main thread; SIGINT's shutdown handler runs on the main thread too, synchronously (setting `_stop_event`, then calling `connector.leave()` which blocks until the browser tears down). While the handler is running, the loop is frozen wherever it was — often inside `read_chat()` or `get_participant_count()`'s `result_q.get(timeout=N)`. When the handler returns control to the loop, the blocked call resumes and returns its result. The loop body then runs through to completion (logging participant count changes, etc.) *before* the top-of-while check re-reads `_stop_event`. Symptom: a stray `ChatRunner: participant count changed X → 0` log appearing several seconds *after* `MacOSAdapter: left meeting`, attributed to the drained queue returning 0. Fix: `if self._stop_event.is_set(): break` immediately after any blocking call in `_loop` (`read_chat`, `get_participant_count`) so the loop bails before processing results from a mid-shutdown unblock.
- **Google Meet leaves the "Admit N guest" pill widget sticky in the DOM after the guest is admitted** (session 115). The pill stays visible (`is_visible() == True`, not hidden, not detached) with the same "Admit 1 guest" text even after a successful tray click admits the knocker. Symptom: an admission verifier that waits for the pill to disappear loops forever; a polling loop that re-attempts whenever the pill is visible spams admission clicks (and any "log success unconditionally after action" code path emits false-positive `admitted via X` lines every poll cycle). Two cooperating fixes in `connectors/macos_adapter.py` admission block: (1) verify success via **participant-count delta** — call `_do_get_participant_count(page)` for up to 3s after the click; if it goes up, that's the real admission signal. (2) **Cooldown** keyed on `(pill_text, participant_count)` — if the next 2s tick sees both unchanged, silently skip; re-attempt only fires when text or count changes (new knocker, someone leaves). Don't try to detect admission via the pill itself.
- **`LLMClient` and the captions path can hold different `MeetingRecord` instances if you forget to call `set_record`** (session 101). When `__main__.py` constructs `LLMClient` *before* `meeting_record` exists (which is what the captions path does — record needs the URL, LLM doesn't), the LLM is left holding its default empty in-memory `MeetingRecord(slug=None)`. `ChatRunner.__init__` only auto-wires `llm.set_record(record)` *inside* the `if self._record is None` branch (chat_runner.py:66-72) — i.e. only when ChatRunner had to construct the record itself. Captions path pre-creates the record → ChatRunner skips the wire → LLM reads from the empty record → `_tail_messages` returns `[]` → Anthropic 400 `messages: at least one message is required`. Symptom: every `@brainchild` call fails the moment captions are enabled. Fix: explicitly `llm.set_record(meeting_record)` immediately after `meeting_record = MeetingRecord(...)` in `__main__.py` (line 218). Diagnostic tell in startup logs: two `MeetingRecord opened …` lines for the same run, one in-memory and one on-disk.
- **Google Meet keeps prior caption text visible in the same speaker's region; same-speaker continuations need fuzzy prefix dedupe** (session 101). Each finalize re-emits whatever Meet hasn't scrolled off yet, so without dedupe the JSONL accumulates `"prior + new"` for every continuation. Strict `text.lower().startswith(prior.lower())` is too brittle — Meet auto-corrects casing/punctuation on already-shown text between finalizes (e.g. `"here,"` → `"Here."`). The voice branch (`voice-preserved/pipeline/captions.py`) already had `_normalize_for_match` for the same problem (echo-suspect detection). Ported as `_strip_prior_prefix(text, prior)` in `pipeline/transcript.py`: tokenize both via `\w+` regex (case + punct insensitive), check token-level prefix match, cut the original text at the end-position of the last matched token. Per-speaker dict so A's prior never affects B. Test coverage in `tests/test_transcript_dedupe.py`. Edge case still uncovered: if Meet rolls the pane such that prior is no longer at the start (only its tail overlaps the new text's head), prefix match fails and duplicate words emit; would need longest-overlap search.
- **`page.expose_function` must precede `page.goto`** (session 99, captions port). Playwright's expose_function registers a Python-callable on `window.*` that the page's JS can invoke. If the observer JS runs before expose_function is registered, `window.__onCaption(...)` is undefined and captions silently drop — no error, no log. Sequencing requirement: in `MacOSAdapter._browser_session`, the expose_function call happens immediately after `browser.pages[0]` and *before* `page.goto(meeting_url, ...)`. **Resolved in session 100 via late-bind:** the bridge expose + observer inject are now gated on `config.CAPTIONS_ENABLED` (not on whether a callback is set), and the Python-side `_on_caption_from_js` stub drops captions when `_caption_callback is None`. `set_caption_callback(fn)` can therefore be called before OR after `join()` — calendar mode wires its per-meeting finalizer once a URL arrives. Tests in `tests/test_caption_late_bind.py` cover the late-bind, swap, unregister, and exception-tolerance cases.
- **Competitive landscape and positioning constraints** (session 97). Primary near-peer: [joinly](https://github.com/joinly-ai/joinly) — multi-platform (Meet/Zoom/Teams), MCP-shaped middleware, BYOLLM (OpenAI/Anthropic/Ollama), voice + chat, MIT licensed, hosted cloud option, shipped 6+ months ago. They're ahead on surface (voice, multi-platform, web UI, dashboard) but weak on specificity (their pitch is "make meetings accessible to AI agents" — abstract; Reddit response was meager). Brainchild's two chosen differentiators: (1) "Claude Code in your Google Meet" framing via Phase 11.5 skill import, (2) opinionated quickstart via `agents/` gallery + `brainchild setup` wizard. **Don't feature-match joinly** — voice, Zoom, Teams, web UI are deliberately out of the MVP. Fight on positioning and seeded community signal instead. Also note Pika (presentation layer, no tool use) and Recall.ai (infra, no agent). Full strategy in `docs/mvp-bar.md`.
- **Large blobs in history block GitHub push indefinitely** (session 93). Repo had two `.onnx` voice benchmark files (60MB + 109MB) buried in mid-history commits — `benchmarks/results/piper_models/` AND a duplicate set at `bench_results/piper_models/`. GitHub rejects any push containing a blob >100MB even if the file is deleted at the tip, because `git push` sends the whole object set. Deleting the files at HEAD doesn't help. Fix: `pip install git-filter-repo` then `git-filter-repo --path-glob '<pattern>' --invert-paths --force`, then re-add origin (filter-repo removes remotes as a safety measure), then `git push --force origin main`. `--force-with-lease` rejects after a history rewrite; plain `--force` is needed. Always check for multiple paths — the duplicate `bench_results/` set was found on a second grep pass after the first rewrite.
- **Whisper drops first word** without 0.5s silence pad prepended to audio. Never remove.
- **Backchannel echo:** clips play through BlackHole → back into capture. Drain audio buffer after playback.
- **Wake phrase is "brainchild" only.** "hey brainchild" rejected (Whisper drops "hey"); "operate" rejected (false positives).
- **ElevenLabs requires paid plan** — free tier gets flagged for abuse.
- **Real Chrome required on macOS** (not Playwright's bundled "Chrome for Testing") — only real Chrome gets mic permission.
- **20s conversation mode timeout** — after response, stays in listening mode 20s before idle.
- **ScreenCaptureKit requires `.app` bundle** on macOS — silently fails from plain Python script.
- **ScreenCaptureKit TCC entries are tied to codesign identity** — if the `audio_capture` binary is recompiled without a stable `--identifier`, macOS generates a hash-based identity. After a TCC reset or macOS update, the old identity's permission entry becomes stale — `startCapture` silently hangs forever. Fix: always sign with `codesign --force --sign - --identifier com.brainchild.audio-capture audio_capture` after compiling.
- **ScreenCaptureKit phantom hang (March 2026):** `startCapture` hung despite permission being on. Root cause: macOS `tccd` cached a stale permission denial. Recovery: (1) `tccutil reset ScreenCapture`, (2) full system restart.
- **Chrome SingletonLock stale after unclean shutdown** — MacOSAdapter pre-launch cleanup removes it automatically. SIGTERM handlers and try/finally blocks prevent it in most cases.
- **Do NOT auto-re-sign `audio_capture` at runtime** — changes code identity, invalidates TCC grant, causes cascading failures.
- **PyObjC packages are fragile** — never install new `pyobjc-framework-*` without checking prior issues.
- **`WHISPER_HALLUCINATIONS` filter** — catches common false positives on silence. Add patterns as found.
- **Audio output device is BlackHole only on macOS** — do NOT change to Multi-Output Device.
- **Ghost session in Meet:** Closing browser without clicking Leave leaves bot registered. Fix: `leave()` must click Leave before `browser.close()`. Handle "Switch here" as fallback.
- **Headless Chrome suppresses audio rendering:** Never use `headless=True`. Use `headless=False` + `--headless=new` on macOS, `headless=False` against Xvfb on Linux.
- **`requestAnimationFrame` is suppressed in `--headless=new`:** Use `setTimeout(fn, 0)` instead. This broke the entire caption MutationObserver pipeline.
- **Google Meet guest join — residential vs. data center IPs:** Residential IPs get guest join. Data center IPs get blocked. Fix for cloud: use exported session via `scripts/auth_export.py`.
- **PulseAudio must be started before Python.** `pulse_setup.sh` creates virtual sinks first.
- **PulseAudio default routing:** Must set default sink/source after creating virtual devices.
- **Chrome does not enumerate PulseAudio monitor sources as microphones.** Use `module-virtual-source` wrapper named `VirtualMic`.
- **PulseAudio user mode (not --system) on droplets.** Add `--exit-idle-time=-1`.
- **Chrome `--no-sandbox` required when running as root.**
- **Playwright `env=` replaces full environment** — never pass it; set env vars in caller.
- **Chrome 130+ uses PipeWire by default** — add `--disable-features=WebRTCPipeWireCapturer` to force PulseAudio.
- **Kokoro 0.9.4 requires spaCy `en_core_web_sm`** — install directly if pip not on PATH.
- **Shift+C is a caption TOGGLE** — check state before pressing. Blind retries toggle on/off/on/off.
- **Join button sequential timeout wastes 5s** — race all three buttons with `.or_()`.
- **HF Hub warning comes from child logger** — suppress both parent and `huggingface_hub.utils._http`.
- **Playwright teardown can hang 20s+** — use `_browser_closed` event, don't join the thread.
- **`_shutdown()` double-call on Ctrl+C** — guard with `_shutdown_called` flag.
- **Browser cleanup must run on ALL exit paths** — wrap in try/finally inside `with sync_playwright()`.
- **Camera toggle needs wait even in headless** — use `wait_for(timeout=5000)`, then confirm via `data-is-muted="true"`.
- **`in_meeting_wait` required before caption enable** — Meet needs transition time after join.
- **Kokoro voice `am_cloud` does not exist** — use `am_michael` or `am_puck` for American Male.
- **Ctrl+C → Chrome stays in meeting 60s (three issues):** (1) rumps swallows SIGINT, (2) SIGINT kills Chrome via process group — fix with `start_new_session=True`, (3) `browser.close()` ≠ leaving — navigate to `about:blank` first.
- **Google Meet and Calendar use different session scopes** — `auth_export.py` must visit both `accounts.google.com` and `calendar.google.com`.
- **Playwright `headless=True` vs `--headless=new` — different cookie stores.** Calendar poller must use `headless=False` + `--headless=new`.
- **LLM round-trip is 0.9–3s** — mask with backchannels, don't try to eliminate.
- **Filler echo after abort causes speaker-change hang.** Fix: `filler_done.wait()` before resuming captions + 3s timeout on `spec.ready.wait()`.
- **`capture_start` timing crack drops late captions.** Fix: check live `_current_text` before entering new capture cycles.
- **Google ASR rewrites captions between speculative and finalization.** Fix: `_normalize_for_match()` canonicalizes both sides.
- **Abort text-grew false positive from wake phrase prefix.** Fix: use `endswith` comparison.
- **Splitting speculative events exposes TTS regression.** Fix: separate `llm_done`/`ready` checks with in-flight TTS detection.
- **Filler echo infinite loop via Meet speaker misattribution.** Fix: dynamic grace period + `allow_abort=False` on retries.
- **Abort path reads stale `_current_text` during `is_speaking`.** Fix: update text/speaker even during speaking + 0.5s settle delay.
- **Caption punctuation triggers false INCOMPLETE.** Fix: `_strip_mid_punctuation()` before classifier.
- **ASR cosmetic rewrites during `is_speaking` trigger false aborts.** Fix: normalize at abort trigger point.
- **Log string truncation mimics data bugs.** Fix: metadata at INFO, full payload at DEBUG.
- **Abort re-fire duplicates prompt.** Fix: use `_current_text` directly, not concatenation.
- **Bot TTS misattributed to human speaker.** Fix: continuity guard + echo fingerprinting.
- **Stored `_wake_position` invalidated by ASR corrections.** Fix: removed — send full caption text.
- **Daemon classifier threads accumulate as zombies.** Fix: `playback_done` event with 50ms polling.
- **Playback interrupt classifier reads stale text.** Fix: `_abort_text` field set at abort time.
- **Caption hallucinations trigger false playback aborts.** Fix: gate through stream classification.
- **INCOMPLETE race condition loses speech during classifier call.** Fix: streaming first-token classification.
- **MacOSAdapter browser.close() outside `with sync_playwright()` silently fails.** The Playwright connection is torn down when the `with` block exits. If `browser.close()` runs in a `finally` outside that scope, it throws and the browser may not close cleanly. Fix: move the try/finally inside the `with` block, matching CaptionsAdapter's pattern.
- **`time.sleep()` in Playwright hold loop blocks the event loop.** JS callbacks (expose_function, MutationObserver) won't fire. Use `page.wait_for_timeout()` instead — it yields to Playwright's event loop while waiting.
- **Playwright is single-threaded (greenlet).** `send_chat()`/`read_chat()` called from the main thread crash with "Cannot switch to a different thread". Fix: queue commands from main thread, execute them in the browser thread's idle loop. Both adapters use `_chat_queue` + `_process_chat_queue()`.
- **Google Meet chat button is a toggle.** "Chat with everyone" opens AND closes the panel. Clicking it when already open closes it, hiding the textarea. Fix: `_ensure_chat_open()` checks textarea visibility before clicking.
- **Google Meet chat selectors (verified April 2026, hardened session 62):** Chat button: `get_by_role("button", name="Chat with everyone")`. Input: `textarea[aria-label="Send a message"]`. Messages: `div[data-message-id]`. Message text: `div[jsname]` (any jsname value, with fallback to first child text node) — previously hardcoded to `jsname="dTKtvb"`. Chat panel: dynamically discovered via `textarea.closest('[data-panel-id]')` — previously hardcoded to `data-panel-id="2"`. Send button: `aria-label="Send a message"` (disabled until text entered; use `fill()` + `Enter` instead).
- **Google Meet chat sender name is in a group header, not per-message.** Sender div found by walking up to 4 parents and matching sibling divs whose text contains a time pattern (`/\d{1,2}:\d{2}\s*(AM|PM)/i`). Format: `"SenderName\nTimestamp"` for other participants, just `"Timestamp"` for the browser's own messages. Previously used obfuscated class `div.HNucUd` — replaced with structural time-pattern approach in session 62. Important: use a `foundSender` flag to stop walking on first match, because empty sender (self-message) is falsy and would cause the loop to keep walking into other message groups.
- **Playwright xpath locator silently returns 0 results for sibling selectors.** `el.locator("xpath=../div[...]")` didn't work for finding sibling elements in the Meet chat DOM. Fix: use `el.evaluate()` with native JS `parentElement.querySelector()` instead.
- **`\b` regex word boundary doesn't match `/` prefix.** If the wake phrase is `/brainchild`, `\bbrainchild\b` won't match because `/` is not a word character. Fix: use `re.escape()` without `\b` anchors.
- **MCP SDK's `stdio_client` uses anyio task groups — cannot split across coroutines.** Manually calling `__aenter__` on `stdio_client` from a separate coroutine (via `run_coroutine_threadsafe`) fails with "Attempted to exit cancel scope in a different task." Fix: each server must run as a single long-lived async task (`_ServerHandle._run()`) that enters the `stdio_client` context and stays alive until shutdown. Tool calls are dispatched to the same event loop via `run_coroutine_threadsafe` to the `_execute_tool` coroutine (which shares the task's session but runs as a separate coroutine — that's fine, the constraint is on the context manager, not the session).
- **`@linear/mcp-server` npm package does not exist.** Linear's official MCP server is remote at `https://mcp.linear.app/mcp`. Use `npx -y mcp-remote https://mcp.linear.app/mcp` to bridge it as a stdio subprocess. Auth is OAuth (browser popup on first run), token cached locally by `mcp-remote`. No `LINEAR_API_KEY` needed.
- **MacOSAdapter/LinuxAdapter "joined" before admission.** Clicking "Ask to join" set `joined = True` immediately without waiting for the host to admit. Brainchild proceeded to open chat panel while still in the waiting room. Fix: track `clicked_label`, and if "Ask to join" was clicked, call `_wait_for_admission()` (two-phase event-driven: wait for lobby image to appear, then watch for it to disappear). Already existed in CaptionsAdapter.
- **Google Meet creates 2 DOM elements per chat message (different IDs, same text).** When Brainchild sends a message, the MutationObserver catches both elements. If the echo filter (`_own_messages`) discards the text on the first match, the second element slips through and triggers an echo loop. Fix: batch the discard — collect matched texts during the full message batch, then remove from `_own_messages` after the loop.
- **Camera toggle must be confirmed before join.** Meet defaults to camera on at the pre-join screen. The old race-both-states approach with a 2s timeout silently skipped the toggle on slow renders. Fix (session 62): click "Turn off camera", then wait for `data-is-muted="true"` on the camera button as confirmation. Log WARNING + screenshot if confirmation fails. No post-join re-check — gate it at pre-join.
- **Meet camera/mic toggles are `<div role="button">`, not `<button>`.** CSS selectors like `button[data-is-muted="true"]` silently match nothing. Use `[role="button"][data-is-muted="true"]` instead. This applies to all Meet toolbar controls.
- **`[data-participant-id]` counts UI elements, not participants.** Returns ~2× actual count due to duplicate DOM entries per participant. Use `[data-requested-participant-id]` instead — reliably matches actual in-call participants (tested: 1-on-1, multi-participant, participant leave, invited-but-absent).
- **Calendar poller joins meetings that ended hours ago.** `minutes_until <= JOIN_WINDOW_MINUTES` has no lower bound — a meeting that started 103 minutes ago has `minutes_until = -103.3`, which is `<= 2`. Fix: extract event end time and skip meetings where `now > end_dt`.
- **`run_polling()` re-join on Ctrl+C.** After `run()` returns, the loop called `_stop_event.clear()` then checked the queue — but the second meeting URL was already queued, so it tried to join mid-shutdown. Fix: check `_stop_event.is_set()` before clearing and looping back.
- **In-meeting participant detection: `innerText` vs `aria-label`.** `[data-participant-id]` elements carry participant names in `innerText` in normal view but NOT in portrait mode. `aria-label` attributes (e.g., "More options for Jojo Shapiro") survive all layouts. Fix: check aria-label first, innerText as fallback.
- **Camera `data-is-muted` flaps during stream acquisition (session 85).** On the Meet pre-join screen, the camera button's `data-is-muted` attribute briefly reports `"true"` before the camera media stream is acquired, then flips to `"false"` once the stream is live. A short poll for `data-is-muted="true"` right after hydration will catch that transient and falsely conclude "camera already off," skipping the toggle click — bot walks in with camera ON. Never use `data-is-muted` as the pre-click "already off" oracle. Two acceptable strategies: (a) always click the "Turn off camera" locator unconditionally (current approach — the button's very existence implies camera is on), then confirm post-click via `data-is-muted="true"` (reliable once stream is settled); or (b) read the button's aria-label as the pre-click oracle (`"Turn off camera"` = on, `"Turn on camera"` = off) — aria-label doesn't flap.
- **Meet participant-tile mic icon lags behind actual mute state on admission (session 85).** When a newly admitted participant joins, remote viewers see a "muted" icon on the participant's video tile for ~1–2 seconds, then it flips to unmuted. This reflects Meet's server-side audio-stream negotiation, NOT the participant's client-side mute button. Diagnostic sampling at t+0.5s / t+1s / t+2s post-admission confirmed the mic button's `aria-label` stays `"Turn off microphone"` and `data-is-muted="false"` throughout. If a user reports the bot appearing briefly muted on entry, no code fix is needed — it's a cosmetic Meet UI lag, not a real mute.
- **Shutdown blocks 14s after browser closes.** `read_chat()` and `get_participant_count()` queue commands for the browser thread. After browser closes, the browser thread stops processing, so callers block until their `result_q.get(timeout=...)` expires (10s + 5s). Fix: drain pending queue commands in the browser thread's finally block, responding with empty results so callers unblock immediately.
- **Ctrl+C during waiting room leaves Chrome running ~60s.** The browser cleanup `finally` only wrapped the in-meeting hold loop. Early returns from auth failure, no join button, or admission cancel/timeout skipped `browser.close()` entirely. With `start_new_session=True` (needed so terminal SIGINT doesn't kill Chrome directly), Chrome outlives Python and stays in the meeting until Meet's heartbeat times out. Fix: lift the `try/finally` to start right after `self._page = page` so all exit paths go through cleanup. Also make `leave()` idempotent (guard on `_leave_event.is_set()`) since both `_shutdown()` and ChatRunner/AgentRunner call it.
- **Deprecated npm `@modelcontextprotocol/server-github` (v0.6.2) fails `search_code` with "Authentication Failed".** The npm package doesn't pass the auth token for the code search endpoint. Other tools like `get_file_contents` work fine. Fix: replaced with official Go binary from `github/github-mcp-server` releases (v0.32.0). The Go binary expects `GITHUB_PERSONAL_ACCESS_TOKEN` (not `GITHUB_TOKEN`).
- **OpenAI parallel tool_calls crash ChatRunner.** When the model returns 2+ tool_calls in one assistant message, `ask()` only returns the first one. The assistant message (with all tool_call_ids) is appended to history, but only one tool result is sent back. OpenAI rejects this with 400: "tool_call_ids did not have response messages." Fix: `parallel_tool_calls=False` in the LLM request. Full parallel support would require ChatRunner to handle multiple confirmations per response.
- **`send_tool_result` must pass tools for follow-up tool calls.** Without `tools` in the kwargs, the LLM can't request another tool call after the first one completes. It emits a text summary instead ("now retrieving auth.py") but can't actually do it. Fix: pass `tools` and `parallel_tool_calls=False` to the completion call in `send_tool_result`, and handle both text and tool_call responses.
- **GitHub MCP `get_file_contents` returns file content as `EmbeddedResource`, not text.** The MCP result has two content parts: a text part ("successfully downloaded text file (SHA: ...)") and an `EmbeddedResource` part containing the actual file content in `c.resource.text`. If you only extract `c.text`, you get the 81-char confirmation and the LLM hallucinates the file contents. Fix: check `hasattr(c, "resource")` and extract `c.resource.text`.
- **Confirmation handler substring matching causes false cancellations.** `any(w in lower for w in ("no", ...))` does substring matching — "know" triggers "no", "token" triggers "ok". Broke tool confirmation flow when users gave natural-language responses containing these substrings. Fix: word-boundary matching via `re.findall(r"\b\w+\b")` for affirmatives only; all non-affirmative responses cancel and pass full user message to LLM for interpretation. Don't try to detect negatives — only detect clear affirmatives.
- **Over-directing MCP hints cause worse LLM behavior than no hints.** Hints like "never call list_issues without a filter" force the LLM to silently add `assignee='me'` to broad queries like "show me all open issues." The `tool_result_max_chars` truncation at `llm.py:203` already catches oversized results and tells the LLM to narrow scope. Hints should address things the LLM can't figure out on its own (status ID ambiguity, binary file poison, index delays) — not prescribe parameter choices the user should be making.
- **GitHub Code Search doesn't index small/new repos.** `search_code` with `repo:dufis1/demo-api` returns 0 results even for code that definitely exists. GitHub's code search indexing is unreliable for repos with few stars/activity. Fix: steer the LLM away from `search_code` toward browsing with `get_file_contents` on directories. System prompt hint: "Avoid search_code — it often returns no results for small repos."
- **LLM uses chat display name as GitHub owner.** When the chat sender is "Jojo Shapiro", gpt-4.1-mini guesses `owner='Jojo'` for GitHub API calls, causing 404s. The `get_me` tool returns the correct login but the model doesn't reliably call it. Fix: resolve `get_me` once at startup in `MCPClient.resolve_github_user()`, inject the login into the LLM system prompt via `inject_github_user()`.
- **Network-loss grace period must be measured from first detection, not polling clock.** If the hold loop polls every 30s for network loss and the drop happens near the end of a cycle, the next poll (30s later) immediately sees 30s elapsed and exits — making the "grace period" anywhere from 0s to 60s. Fix: track `network_lost_at = time.time()` on the first tick that sees the alert, and only exit when `time.time() - network_lost_at >= GRACE`. Use a faster poll cadence (5s) for the alert check so the first-detection timestamp is accurate to within 5s. The alert disappearing before grace expires resets `network_lost_at = None` (self-heal).
- **`_ServerHandle.stop()` must not cancel the task immediately after setting shutdown event.** `stdio_client`'s `__aexit__` has its own cleanup sequence (close stdin, wait 2s, SIGTERM via `os.killpg`, wait, SIGKILL) that takes ~4s for a stubborn process. Calling `task.cancel()` injects `CancelledError` into that sequence at whatever `await` it's on, aborting cleanup and orphaning the subprocess. Fix: set the event, wait for the task to complete naturally (5s timeout), only cancel as last resort if it hangs.
- **`self._task` in `_ServerHandle` must be set via `asyncio.current_task()` inside `_run()`.** `asyncio.run_coroutine_threadsafe()` returns a `concurrent.futures.Future`, not an `asyncio.Task`. If you store the Future in `self._task`, `task.cancel()` and `await task` won't work (wrong type). And if you don't store anything (as was the case from session 51 to 78), `_cancel_task()` silently skips because `self._task` is `None` — dead code that masks the real shutdown bug.
- **Safety net for child process cleanup: `pgrep -P <pid>` after graceful shutdown.** No single subsystem's cleanup is guaranteed to work in all cases (event loop killed early, library bug, user-added MCP server misbehaves). `_kill_orphaned_children()` at the end of `_shutdown()` enumerates remaining children via `pgrep -P <our_pid>`, SIGTERMs them, waits 0.5s, then SIGKILLs survivors. Works on macOS and Linux, no new dependencies. No recursion needed — all children use `start_new_session=True`, so killing the direct child is sufficient.
- **Python `\n` in JS comments inside `page.evaluate()` breaks the script.** A comment like `// matches "Name\nTimestamp"` in a triple-quoted Python string sends a literal newline to JS, splitting the comment mid-line and causing a SyntaxError. Fix: avoid `\n` in any JS string/comment inside `evaluate()` — use `"Name + Timestamp"` or similar. Same applies to any Python escape sequence that isn't explicitly doubled.
- **Chat MutationObserver silently no-ops if textarea not in DOM at install time.** `_install_chat_observer` injects JS that finds the chat textarea and resolves `textarea.closest('[data-panel-id]')` as the observed container. If the textarea isn't in the DOM yet (panel still rendering), the JS function returns early without setting `window.__brainchildChatObserver` — but `page.evaluate()` doesn't throw, so Python had no way to detect the failure. The old code set `_observer_installed = True` unconditionally and never retried. Fix: (1) after `page.evaluate()`, explicitly check `!!window.__brainchildChatObserver` and only set `_observer_installed = True` on confirmed success; (2) replace the fixed 500ms sleep in `_ensure_chat_open` with `textarea.wait_for(state="visible")` so the panel is confirmed rendered before install is attempted.
- **Falsy empty-string check skips self-message sender match.** When extracting sender name via parent-walk, self-messages return `sender = ''`. If the outer loop uses `if (sender) break`, empty string is falsy — the loop continues walking up and matches a different message group's sender div, returning a wrong name. Fix: use a `foundSender` boolean flag to stop on first time-pattern match regardless of whether sender is empty.
- **Queue-depth warning race at dequeue time.** First attempt at the "overlapping meetings" warning in `run_polling` checked `meeting_queue.qsize() > 0` right before calling `self.run(url)`. This missed the common case: CalendarPoller runs on its own thread and may queue meeting 2 *after* meeting 1 has already been dequeued (observed 5ms gap in a live test, and the typical case is seconds/minutes later while meeting 1 is running). The dequeue-time check is blind to meetings queued after that moment. Fix: moved the warning into `CalendarPoller._check_calendar` where it runs at *enqueue* time on the poller's own thread, with an `is_busy` callback from the runner so it can detect "meeting 1 is running" even when the queue is empty.
- **CalendarPoller "already ended" skip logs re-fire every poll cycle.** Old or multi-day events that have ended still appear in Google Calendar's day view and get re-evaluated on every 30s poll. Without deduplication, they produce DEBUG log lines every cycle, drowning real events. Fix: track `_ended_event_ids` in CalendarPoller and only log the skip the first time each event_id is seen. Note: accessibility labels for multi-day events start with a date (e.g., "April 7, 2026 at 7pm to...") not "All day", so the `startswith("all day")` filter doesn't catch them — they rely on the `end_dt` skip instead. That's fine, just be aware if debugging calendar noise.
- **Google Calendar event accessibility label looks like a timestamp but isn't.** `ev.inner_text()` on an event cell returns a comma-separated blob like `'April 7, 2026 at 7pm to April 8, 2026 at 7:52pm, test 2, Brainchild, Needs RSVP, No location,'`. When this blob appears in a log line next to a local-time Python timestamp like `23:38:02`, it can look like Brainchild thinks the current time is 7pm. It doesn't — that "7pm" is the scheduled start of the event. Just a reading-the-logs gotcha.
- **`wait_for_selector` on an absent selector silently regresses startup.** The original `CalendarPoller` had a blind `time.sleep(8)` after `page.goto()`. Replacing it with `wait_for_selector("[data-eventid]", timeout=15000)` looked obviously better — but on empty-calendar days the selector never appears and the wait runs to the full 15s, making startup *worse* (16.3s vs the original 9.4s). Tighten the timeout to ~3s and accept the no-events path waits 3s of nothing — the next 30s poll picks up any late events anyway. Always test the empty case when replacing a sleep with a selector wait.
- **MCP `get_file_contents` on binary files poisons the entire session.** During GitHub MCP pressure testing (G7), calling `get_file_contents` on a PNG returned the image bytes as an inline `[image]` content block. Once that block was in conversation context, every subsequent API request returned HTTP 400 `"Could not process image"` — including `/exit` and `/end-session`. The image was re-sent on every turn, so the only recovery was `/compact` to drop it from context. The trick was that the failure surfaces on the *next* request, not the tool call itself, so it's easy to misread as a transient API error. Fix (code-level, session 80): two-layer defense in `pipeline/guardrails.py`. Pre-execution: text-extension allowlist blocks `get_file_contents` on non-text paths before the MCP call fires. Post-execution: `validate_tool_result()` scans every tool result for null bytes, base64 image data, and non-printable character ratios before it enters LLM history. The prompt hint was removed — code enforcement is reliable where hints aren't (proven by the `limit` parameter saga).
- **Camera click can return success without toggling state (hydration race).** Playwright's `.click()` on a Meet camera button can return success while the button's JS click handler hasn't been wired up yet — the native click event fires on an inert DOM node and nothing happens. Symptom: "clicked 'Turn off camera'" logs, then `data-is-muted` stays `"false"` through the 3s verification. Indistinguishable from an overlay intercept (where a transparent element absorbs the click) without extra diagnostics. Fix (session 81): wait for the button *with* `data-is-muted` attribute present (true interactivity signal, not just existence) before clicking; on verification failure, fall back to `⌘+E` keyboard shortcut which routes through Meet's global hotkey handler and bypasses both failure modes. Log `_probe_camera_button()` diagnostic (attribute presence, `elementFromPoint`, intercept flag) pre-click and on failure so future occurrences are categorizable.
- **Pre-join wait_for_selector that mixes subsystems returns too early.** The old `wait_for_selector('Join now, Ask to join, Turn off camera, Sign in')` returned as soon as *any* match appeared. Meet hydrates subsystems progressively: join buttons often render before the camera control. A wait that resolves on the join button proceeds to camera interaction while the camera subsystem is still loading. Fix: scope that wait to the join/auth buttons only, and do a separate dedicated wait for the camera control before interacting with it.
- **Anthropic emits parallel tool_use blocks by default (session 90).** Claude Sonnet 4.5 will often return 2+ `tool_use` blocks in a single assistant turn when a query is exploratory (e.g. one scoped + one unscoped `list_issues`). Our `LLMClient.ask()` loop is built around executing one tool_call per turn and feeding back one `tool_result`. If you append the assistant turn to history with both tool_use IDs but only one tool_result, the next request fails with `400: tool_use ids were found without tool_result blocks immediately after: <id>`. Fix: pass `tool_choice={"type": "auto", "disable_parallel_tool_use": True}` to `messages.create` whenever tools are present. Analogous to OpenAI's `parallel_tool_calls=False`. Full parallel support is post-MVP (see roadmap) and requires `LLMClient` to execute N tool_calls per turn.
- **Anthropic input-token rate limits are tiny on Tier 1; prompt caching is opt-in (session 90).** Tier 1 is 30k input-tokens-per-minute for Claude Sonnet. Our setup resends all 72 MCP tool schemas on every LLM call (~20k tokens each), plus system prompt + history, so a single user question (decide-tool → summarize = 2 LLM calls) can blow past 30k ITPM. Unlike OpenAI (which auto-caches any prompt ≥1024 tokens on GPT-4o/4.1), Anthropic caching is opt-in: content must be marked with `cache_control: {"type": "ephemeral"}`, breakpoint at the end of the cacheable prefix. We cache system + all tool schemas by (a) wrapping system as `[{type: text, text, cache_control: ephemeral}]` and (b) adding `cache_control: ephemeral` to the *last* tool in the list. Cached reads cost 10% and pressure the rate limit far less. The ITPM cap resets each minute. 429 handler in `AnthropicProvider.complete()` logs the cap and the tier-upgrade path so users aren't mystified.
- **Anthropic SDK DEBUG logging dumps full request payloads (session 90).** `anthropic._base_client` at DEBUG level prints the entire `Request options` JSON on every call — including all 72 tool schemas and full conversation history. In a chat-mode Meet that's a ~20k-token blob per call flooding stdout. `__main__.py:222` silenced `httpcore/httpx/openai/elevenlabs` but missed `anthropic`. Fix: add `"anthropic"` to the noisy-logger list in both `__main__.py` and `cloud/docker/entrypoint.py`. Anytime a new API SDK is added to the project, audit its DEBUG logging before shipping.
- **Browser profile mtime check via Chromium `Default/Cookies`.** `shutil.copytree` uses `copy2` under the hood, which preserves mtimes. So after a copy, the source and destination `Default/Cookies` have *equal* mtimes — and on the next start, comparing those mtimes is a one-stat shortcut for "has auth state moved on since the last copy?" Used in `CalendarPoller._cal_profile_is_stale` to skip the rmtree+copytree on warm restarts. Don't compare directory mtimes — they only change on entry add/remove, not on file edits.
- **Figma's official MCP catalog gate is hard, not soft (session 112).** `https://mcp.figma.com/mcp` via `mcp-remote` rejects dynamic-client registration with `HTTP 403 Forbidden` at the `registerClient` step — *before* any OAuth consent screen. It's not a scope/permission issue users can approve around; it's a hard allowlist gate on the MCP client itself. Brainchild is not in the catalog. Diagnostic tell: `mcp-remote` log shows `Dynamic client registration failed` with 403, not a browser redirect. Fix: default the designer bundle to GLips (`figma-developer-mcp`, PAT-authenticated, read-only). Revisit only if/when Brainchild is admitted to Figma's catalog.
- **GLips `figma-developer-mcp` is read-only but the README doesn't say so (session 112).** Verified by reading `src/mcp/index.ts` on GitHub: registers exactly two tools (`get_figma_data`, `download_figma_images`), both with `readOnlyHint: true`. No mutation tools exist. If writes are needed, swap to Grab's `cursor-talk-to-figma-mcp` (~25 mutation tools, requires Figma plugin + `bun socket` bridge, loses "paste a Figma URL" UX because it operates only on the file currently open in the plugin). Lesson: verify MCP server capabilities against source, not just README claims.
- **Thin Figma payloads are ground truth, not bugs (session 112).** First test URL returned 592 bytes with a single RECTANGLE node; felt like a truncation bug. Verified against Figma REST API directly (`curl https://api.figma.com/v1/files/<key>`) — the file genuinely contained one rectangle. Brainchild's anti-hallucination guard in the designer hints ("if get_figma_data returns a thin payload, say so plainly and ask for a different node-id — do not fabricate structure") fires correctly in this case. When Designer's critique feels unexpectedly shallow, verify the source frame actually has the structure the user expects before blaming the LLM.
- **Sonnet 4.5 over-triggers `load_skill` on casual prompts (session 112, tuning note).** "Gut check, what's the first thing you'd change?" fired `load_skill("design-review-feedback")` on first attempt — the test plan's own "fail signal" for T5. Redirect prompt ("brief thoughts?") switched the register correctly. Not a bug; a tuning knob. If it becomes a problem, tighten the skill's `description` field (the menu entry) to explicitly exclude casual/gut-check prompts, or raise the skill's bar via system prompt hint. Shipped as-is.
- **`figma-developer-mcp` spawns a grandchild process that survives top-level SIGINT (session 112).** MCP client sends SIGINT to the top-level subprocess (npx shim), which exits. The real `figma-developer-mcp` binary (grandchild via `npx`) doesn't receive the signal and lingers. Our existing `_kill_orphaned_children()` safety net catches it via `pgrep -P <our_pid>` and SIGTERMs it — so user-visible behavior is clean, but logs show "killed orphaned child". Not a regression; this is exactly why the safety net exists (see entry above on child process cleanup). Applies to any npx-wrapped MCP server.
- **`meet.new` URL-resolution trap: the interstitial URL ends with `/new` and has a query string (session 114).** Navigating to `https://meet.new` redirects through `https://meet.google.com/new?authuser=0&hs=178` before landing on the real room `https://meet.google.com/<xxx-xxxx-xxx>`. A lambda like `u.endswith("meet.google.com") == False and "/new" not in u` is not enough — query strings bypass naive path-ending checks. Fix: use `urlparse(u).path` to strip query/fragment and validate with a regex `^/[a-z]{3,}-[a-z]{3,}-[a-z]{3,}/?

 (three hyphen-separated lowercase groups is Meet's room-code shape). Used as the predicate to `wait_for_url`. Symptom when this breaks: the *bot* lands in room A and `webbrowser.open(meeting_url)` hands the human the interstitial URL, which causes Google to spin up a *different* fresh meeting under the human's account — two rooms, no overlap.
- **Google Meet's "Admit N guests" pill is a hover-tray widget, not a button (session 114).** The visible green pill in the top-right when someone knocks is *not* a `<button role="button">` — it's a nested div with aria description "Press Down Arrow to open the hover tray and Escape to close." Clicking the pill element directly doesn't fire Meet's admit handler; you have to open the tray first (via hover or keyboard) and then click the `Admit` button that appears inside the tray. Synthetic `dispatchEvent(new MouseEvent('mouseenter'))` does NOT open the tray — Google's widget is bound to real mouse events. Playwright's `.hover()` does work because it moves the cursor via CDP (real browser-level mouse event). Keyboard path (`pill.focus()` → `ArrowDown` → `Enter`) is the fallback since the aria description explicitly documents it.
- **Playwright `:has-text()` matches ancestors, not just leaves (session 114).** A selector like `:is(button, [role="button"]):has-text("Admit")` seems scoped but actually matches *every ancestor* whose descendant subtree contains the text "Admit" — including body-level containers. In our first auto-admit attempt this over-matched ~20 unrelated elements per poll cycle and (accidentally) triggered unrelated UI like reopening the chat panel. If you need a tight "element whose accessible name IS X" match, use `get_by_role("button", name=re.compile(r"^Admit$", re.I))` instead; `:has-text()` is for content searches across subtrees.
- **Already-in-meeting detection via `Leave call` button (session 114).** When the bot creates a meeting via `meet.new`, Google auto-joins it as the creator — by the time the adapter's pre-join flow starts, the "Join now" / "Ask to join" / "Sign in" buttons don't exist because we're *already in*. The pre-join race times out on all three and the adapter tore down with `join_fail`. Fix: before the pre-join race, probe for `get_by_role("button", name="Leave call")` — if visible, set `clicked_label = "already_in"` and skip both camera toggle and the join-button race. `Leave call` is a reliable "am I in the meeting?" oracle because it only exists during an active call.
- **The bot must stay headless; the human needs a separate visible tab (session 114).** The bot's Chrome runs with `--headless=new` — that's intentional (invisible observer). Don't remove `--headless=new` to "show the browser" — that makes the bot visible, which is wrong. Instead, when the bot auto-creates a meeting (meet.new path), pop a *second* visible tab in the user's default browser via `webbrowser.open(meeting_url)` from `__main__.py`. The bot and human connect to the same room through two different browser sessions. Only call `webbrowser.open` after the room URL is resolved (never pass the interstitial).
- **Rich's markup parser silently swallows `[x]` in toggle lists (session 119).** When rendering a numbered checkbox list in the setup wizard via `rich.console.Console.print()`, `[x]` disappears from output while `[ ]` (space inside) prints literally — asymmetric and easy to miss. Rich treats `[...]` as a style tag; `[x]` matches the "nonexistent style `x`" grammar and gets stripped, but `[ ]` doesn't parse as a valid tag so it survives. Symptom: first smoke-test of `brainchild setup` showed bundled skills as `1. · alpha` instead of `1. [x] alpha`. Fix: use a non-bracket glyph for the "on" mark — `[✓]` for checked, `[ ]` for unchecked. Alternative would be `Console(markup=False)` but that kills other useful formatting. Rule of thumb: anything enclosed in `[…]` that isn't a valid style name is at risk; prefer Unicode glyphs for user-facing status indicators in Rich output.
- **Edit-in-place bundle rewrites must seed the tempdir with the existing bundle first, or unknown files get wiped (session 119).** The `brainchild setup` wizard uses atomic write — build into `agents/.<name>.tmp-<ts>/`, then `os.rename` it over `agents/<name>/` (with a `.bak-<ts>` swap for recovery). First implementation built the tempdir from scratch with only the wizard-owned files (`config.yaml`, `portrait.txt`, `skills/`, stub `README.md`), then swapped. Result: `.env.example`, hand-written README edits, delegate scripts, and any other non-owned siblings in the preset bundle got nuked silently on reconfigure — the user never consented to that. Fix: in `edit` mode, seed the tempdir via `shutil.copytree(target, tmp, dirs_exist_ok=True)` *before* any writes so the full existing bundle carries through the swap. Then selectively overwrite owned files, wipe `skills/` wholesale (skills are re-authored each run), and write `README.md` only if absent. The test `test_edit_in_place_swap_cleans_backup` pins this: asserts `.env.example` + pre-existing README survive, stale `skills/deselected/` is gone, no `.bak-*` lingers on success. Generalizable rule: atomic-write flows that "replace a directory" must preserve any files the operation doesn't explicitly own.

---

## LLM Interaction Principles

Design patterns for working with LLMs in this product. Read before making architectural decisions about context management or model behavior.

- **Archive-with-metadata pattern:** When removing content from the model's context (tool results, history turns), always replace it with a placeholder that names (1) what happened and (2) what the model can do about it. Example: `[tool result archived — call the tool again with a narrower scope to retrieve more]` is better than silent deletion or `[result omitted]` (which implies error). The model reasons better when it understands its own state and has a recovery path. Applies anywhere context is managed: history trimming, tool result truncation, overflow recovery.

---

## To-Do (non-urgent)

- **Sender time-pattern regex assumes AM/PM format.** The structural sender extraction (session 62 hardening) uses `/\d{1,2}:\d{2}\s*(AM|PM)/i` to find the sender div. Breaks in 24h locales where timestamps render as `"22:35"` without AM/PM. Add 24h pattern `\d{2}:\d{2}` as alternative match when locale support matters.
- **Caption speaker badge still uses fragile class selectors.** `.NWpY1d, .xoMHSc` in `captions_adapter.py` are obfuscated CSS classes. Structural fix identified: use `firstElementChild` positional extraction (speaker is always first child in its wrapper). Not v1-critical — captions are post-v1 voice path (Phase 11, steps 11.5–11.8).
- **Revisit LLM history compaction if needed.** Context overflow handling in step 9.11 clears history as a last resort. If long meetings with heavy tool use make this a frequent problem, consider summarizing old turns instead of discarding them (one extra LLM call per compaction). Deferred — meetings are short and 128k context is generous.
- **LLM hallucinated a tool call result instead of calling the tool (session 76).** When creating 4 issues in sequence, the 4th `save_issue` call was never made — the LLM returned a text reply matching the expected success pattern from the prior 3 creates. No `tool_call` in the response, no `MCP executing` in logs, yet the chat message said the issue was created. This is a reliability problem: the model pattern-matched from conversation history rather than executing the tool. Investigate: is this a temperature/sampling issue? Should we detect when a reply claims a tool action was taken but no tool_call was in the response? Could be a guard in ChatRunner.
- ~~**Stale `mcp-remote` process blocks Linear auth on next startup (session 76).**~~ Fixed in session 78. See Hard-Won Knowledge.
