## Phase 11.4 — Skill Loading (design notes)

**History (session 102).** Originally split as 11.4 (generic flat-`.md`) + 11.5 (Claude Code interop on top). Collapsed into a single phase: adopting `SKILL.md` shape + progressive disclosure + `allowed-tools` filtering up front is simpler than shipping twice. `skills.local.yaml` deferred to post-MVP.

Pitch: **"Claude Code in Google Meet."** Users bring their existing Claude Code skills into Brainchild instead of recreating them.

**Source of truth.** Claude Code skills live at `~/.claude/skills/<name>/SKILL.md` (user-level) and `.claude/skills/<name>/SKILL.md` (project-level). Each skill is a folder with a `SKILL.md` — YAML frontmatter (`name`, `description`, optional `allowed-tools`) plus a markdown body. Format is designed for progressive disclosure: only `name + description` loads up front; the full body is pulled in when the model decides the skill is relevant.

**Load model: reference, not copy.** `config.yaml` stores paths (`~/.claude/skills/<name>` or absolute paths), not file contents. On startup, Brainchild reads `SKILL.md` live from the user's machine. Rationale: each user's `~/.claude/skills/` is already their curated, personal set — forcing a copy into the repo would be double-bookkeeping, and the open-source story is "each user makes Brainchild theirs." Downside acknowledged: paths only exist on that user's machine, so a teammate who clones the repo will hit missing skills. Mitigation: log + skip, don't crash.

**Implementation shape.**
- `config.yaml` gains a `skills:` list. Entries are paths (absolute or `~`-expanded). An entry may be either a single skill folder (contains `SKILL.md`) or a parent directory (scanned one level deep for `*/SKILL.md`). Parent-dir scanning is what makes `~/.claude/skills/` a single-line config entry.
- On startup, resolve each path, parse `SKILL.md` frontmatter with `pyyaml` (already a dep).
- **Progressive disclosure.** Inject only `name + description` of each skill into the system prompt as an available-skills list. Register a synthetic `load_skill(name: str)` tool alongside MCP tools. When the model calls it, Brainchild returns the full body of the named skill as the tool result. Model then re-plans with the body in context. Matches Claude Code's loading behavior; keeps token cost flat as users accumulate skills.
- Missing path → WARN log + skip. Do not crash startup.
- Malformed `SKILL.md` (bad YAML, missing `name` / `description`) → WARN log + skip.
- Duplicate skill names across paths → last one wins, WARN on collision.
- Startup log line: `SKILLS: N/M loaded (<name> ✓, <name> ✓, <name> ✗ missing)`. Mirrors the MCP startup banner pattern from session 87.
- **Deferred to post-MVP:** optional gitignored `skills.local.yaml` for personal overrides — teams share a baseline `config.yaml` and layer personal skills on top. Not MVP-critical.
- System prompt ordering: base prompt → skills block → MCP hints → MCP status (most dynamic last, so skills share a stable prefix for prompt caching).

**Tool-surface filtering.** Most interesting Claude Code skills assume tools Brainchild doesn't have in a meeting context. Split by `allowed-tools`:
- **Pure-instruction skills** (no `allowed-tools`, or only MCP-backed tools): ship as-is. Tone guides, commit-message style, decision frameworks, interview rubrics.
- **MCP-backed skills** (Linear, Gmail, Calendar): work once the corresponding MCP server is configured.
- **Tool-heavy skills** (`Bash`, `Edit`, `Write`, `Read`): known to misfire. Five common ones that break: `/commit`-style git skills, the `pdf` skill, the office-suite skill (`docx`/`xlsx`/`pptx`), PR-review skills (`/review-pr`, `simplify`), refactor/debug-test-failure skills. Common thread: **anything that assumes a filesystem, a shell, or the Read/Edit/Write triad** breaks in a Meet context.
- On import, check `allowed-tools`; if it references tools Brainchild can't honor, log a WARN with the specific unsupported tools. Still load the skill (the model may decline to invoke it in the meeting context) but the user knows why it might misfire.

**Out of scope for 11.4.** Skill *execution* beyond injecting body text — i.e., we are not implementing `Bash`/`Edit`/`Write`/`Read` to make tool-heavy skills actually work. Pitch is honest: "bring your instruction skills." Also out of scope: hot-reload when a `SKILL.md` changes on disk mid-meeting — load at startup only (restart required for changes).

---

## Phase 15.5 — Opinionated Quickstart (design notes)

Pitch: **"Choose your fighter → add power-ups → go."** The agents gallery is the gallery layer; the wizard turns it into a 3-step setup. Implicit differentiator vs. joinly's framework-shaped positioning.

**Why a gallery, not forks.** Forks fragment git history and don't make the parent repo look alive. A `roster/` folder with PR contributions keeps everyone on main, makes contributors visible in the commit log, and turns every seeded-persona build into a permanent artifact. This is the primitive; forks were rejected explicitly. Reference patterns: Ollama model library, LangChain templates, n8n templates, ComfyUI workflows, Vercel templates, Hugging Face Spaces.

**Folder format (already locked in `roster/README.md`).** Each roster member is a self-contained folder with a runnable `config.yaml`, optional `skills/` directory, a short `README.md` (what / who / needs / setup / demo), and `.env.example`. The roster member must run on a fresh clone after the user fills in keys — no hidden dependencies.

### 15.5.1 — `claude-code` starter agent

Canonical example. Demonstrates the format and is the launch hero. **Depends on Phase 11.5 (Claude Code skill import) being complete** — without skill import, this agent has nothing distinct to show.

- `roster/engineer/config.yaml` — complete Brainchild config; either OpenAI or Anthropic as default (decide near build time, lean Anthropic since the framing is "Claude Code"); `mcp_servers` includes Linear + GitHub; `skills:` points at `~/.claude/skills/` by default, with a comment explaining how to swap to a custom path.
- `roster/engineer/README.md` — "What it does: brings your existing `~/.claude/skills/` into Google Meet so the agent files Linear tickets, looks up GitHub PRs, and follows your team conventions during a live call." Setup: copy `config.yaml`, fill `.env`, run. Demo: short GIF of an artifact appearing in chat mid-sentence.
- `roster/engineer/skills/` — leave empty by default. The whole point is the user's own skills get loaded from `~/.claude/skills/`. Optionally bundle one demo skill that's safe to ship (e.g. `file-linear-ticket.md`) so the agent has at least one skill even if the user has none locally.
- `.env.example` — `OPENAI_API_KEY` or `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`, `LINEAR_API_KEY`, `GITHUB_TOKEN`.

### 15.5.3 — Runtime architecture (roster as source of truth)

**The architectural shift** (session 113): today, `python __main__.py <url>` reads an ambient `config.yaml` at repo root — "whatever was last copied there." Replaced by explicit per-run bot selection. Every run names the bot.

- Positional CLI in `__main__.py`:
  - `brainchild <name> <url>` — run that bot in that meeting. Load `roster/<name>/config.yaml` directly.
  - `brainchild <name>` (no URL) — auto-open `meet.new`, capture slug, join as that bot. (Absorbs old 15.5.4's `meet.new` deliverable.)
  - `brainchild setup` — launches the wizard (see 15.5.5).
  - `brainchild list` — prints available roster members + one-line pitches.
  - `brainchild` (bare) — prints usage + roster list.
- Dispatch rule: if first arg matches a `roster/*` folder, treat as bot-name; if it's a known subcommand (`setup` / `list`), dispatch there; else error with helpful usage.
- Delete root `config.yaml`. Config loading reads `roster/<name>/config.yaml` at runtime.
- `.env` stays at repo root, shared across all bots (keys like `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` are environment-scoped, not bot-scoped).
- Ship `./brainchild` bash wrapper in repo root: `#!/usr/bin/env bash` + `cd "$(dirname "$0")"` + `source venv/bin/activate` + `exec python __main__.py "$@"`. Provisional launcher until product name is locked and curl installer ships post-launch.
- **Breaking change:** every doc, test, and reference to `python __main__.py <url>` migrates to `brainchild <name> <url>`. Pre-launch, so the cost is grep + update, not deprecation.

### 15.5.4 — Face system + profile banner

Each bot has a unique pixel-art face that prints on every run. Faces are the bot's identity and the "you're playing as X" moment when a meeting starts.

- **Deterministic face generator.** Half-block Unicode (`▀ ▄ █`) + ANSI 256-color. 16×20 pixels — fits 3-across in a standard terminal, readable. Seed = hash(bot name), so the same name always produces the same face. Parts library: eyes, mouth, brow, hair/hat, accessory, palette.
- **Shipping portraits.** Run the generator for `engineer` / `pm` / `designer`, hand-curate until good, commit as `roster/<name>/portrait.txt`.
- **First-run write hook.** Any `brainchild <name>` run that finds no `portrait.txt` in the roster folder generates one and writes it. This is the "gift" for contributors: they add `roster/translator/` with a config and README, run `brainchild translator` once, and a face file materializes for them to commit with their PR.
- **Startup banner.** Every `brainchild <name>` run prints a block before joining:
  ```
  ╔════════════════════════════╗
  ║   <face>      ENGINEER     ║
  ║               looks up GH  ║
  ║               MCPs: GitHub ║
  ║               Skills: 4    ║
  ║               Model: ...   ║
  ╚════════════════════════════╝
  ```
  Reads from the active config — pulls agent name, one-line tagline (from README h1 or a config field), MCP names, skill count, model.
- **`--plain` fallback.** Prints ASCII-only banner for screen readers / hostile terminals / CI logs.
- Dep: `rich` for color/boxes/layout (new dep — already battle-tested, 1-package install).

### 15.5.5 — `brainchild setup` wizard (creation flow)

**Key reframe** (session 113): wizard is no longer "activate a bundle by copying config to root." It's a *creation* tool — builds a new `roster/<name>/` folder so the user ends up with their own bot they run explicitly.

- `brainchild setup` — four steps:
  1. **Choose a template (or start blank).** Fighter-select grid UI — colored boxes, pre-shipped faces visible, numbered prompt. "Start blank" produces a minimal config stub.
  2. **Power-ups — awareness + toggle.** Show the template's bundled MCPs and skills as a checklist (including commented-out power-up entries in the template config). User toggles what ends up in the new bot. Narrow scope: only touches what the template declares. Out of scope: arbitrary MCP discovery, paste-a-URL flow, `~/.claude/skills` path editor (all post-launch).
  3. **Keys.** Prompt for any env vars the new bot needs that aren't already in `.env`. `getpass` for secrets (no echo, never print existing values). Merge into `.env`, preserving unrelated keys. Atomic write.
  4. **Finalize.** Atomic-write the new `roster/<new-name>/` folder: `config.yaml` (built from template + toggles), `README.md` stub, `.env.example`. Generate face via 15.5.4's generator, write `portrait.txt`. Print: `Your bot is ready. Run: brainchild <new-name> <meet-url>`.
- Re-run-safe: name-collision check against existing roster folders.
- Intent of step 2: pure FYI — user should *know* what their bot can do (so they know to ask it to file a Linear ticket), not be forced into configuration work. Checkbox ergonomics, not a forms-based MCP configurator.
- **Depends on 15.5.3** (for `setup` dispatch surface) and **15.5.4** (for face generator + pre-baked shipping portraits rendered in step 1's grid).
- ~250 lines of Python + `rich`. Out of scope: voice, MCP OAuth flows, model selection UI beyond what the template dictates. Those land in the post-MVP full wizard.

### Launch interplay

The gallery doubles as launch ammunition (see `docs/mvp-bar.md` Launch Strategy). Each seeded persona contributes one `roster/<name>/` PR, then posts about that build. Real users browsing the repo see contributor activity on `main` — social proof as code. Ship 3 roster members at launch (engineer + PM + designer), target 5 within week 1 via seeded PRs.

---

## Phase 15.7 — MCP Hardening + Team Completion (design notes)

*Session 147 approval — six sub-phases sequenced between Phase 14.8 clean-mac smoke and Phase 15.1 Linux. Full roadmap entry at `docs/roadmap.md` Phase 15.7.*

### Motivation
- Three shipped agents + three shipped skills (prd-from-discussion, standup-summary, design-review-feedback) ≠ a **team**. The skills don't yet tell a complete arc from meeting → artifact. Engineer ships with zero bundled skills; Designer only covers aesthetic review.
- Adding 5 new MCPs onto a codebase that only handles missing-creds via `/tmp/brainchild.log` warnings is a liability — every new MCP multiplies the surface for "enabled-but-unauthed" mid-meeting silence. Hardening must land before breadth.
- Target persona (remote teams with AI in meetings, not just solo founders) — the win is a self-evident "cool, I didn't realize it could do that" moment during `brainchild setup` skill picker + a corresponding moment in the meeting itself.

### The arc we're closing
`prd-from-discussion` (PM, shipped) → `design-handoff-spec` (Designer, new) → `scope-estimate` (Engineer, new) → delegate_to_claude_code → `pr-review` (Engineer, new) → `live-bug-triage` (Engineer, new, Sentry-backed) → `release-notes` (Engineer, new) → `standup-summary` (PM, shipped) → `schedule-followup` (PM, new, Calendar-backed). That's every relay-runner in a feature's life getting a meeting-native moment.

### Hardening — the four phases A–D land in this order because each compounds
- **15.7.1 (A) error classification** ✅ (session 148, `6beff98`) — `_resolve_env_vars` returns `(resolved, missing_vars)`; `_classify_startup_failure` returns structured `{kind, fix, raw, [vars]}` with `missing_creds` taking precedence over any noisier crash; rename `failed_servers` → `startup_failures`, `disabled_servers` → `runtime_failures`, both now `dict[str, dict]`. `record_tool_result` accepts `error_text` and upgrades tripped servers to `kind="auth_failed"` when any sub-threshold failure matched `_AUTH_ERROR_PATTERNS` (empirical: GitHub "Bad credentials", Figma "Forbidden", plus documented Slack/Sentry/Salesforce/Google patterns). Empirical capture script lives at `tests/probe_auth_errors.py`; results archived in `docs/mcp-auth-errors.md`.
- **15.7.2 (B) proactive banner** ✅ (session 148, `43dae3f`) — `ChatRunner._post_mcp_failure_banner` in `run()` posts one compact line after `ui.ok("Joined meeting…")`, BEFORE the async intro thread so it lands deterministically even if intro generation errors. `_FAILURE_KIND_LABELS` dispatches per `kind`; multi-failure joins with "; " + "Ask for details." Silent when `startup_failures` is empty.
- **15.7.3 (C) OAuth decoupling** ✅ (session 148, `ed63026`) — new `auth: env \| oauth` field + `auth_url` on MCP blocks; `_oauth_cache_exists(auth_url)` checks `~/.mcp-auth/mcp-remote-*/<md5(auth_url)>_tokens.json` (lex-latest version dir). `connect_all` runs the pre-check before spawning auth:oauth servers — missing → skip + `kind="oauth_needed"`. New `brainchild auth <mcp>` CLI subcommand foreground-spawns the configured command+args with stdin piped + stdout/stderr inherited, polls for tokens.json, SIGTERMs on success. Bundled Linear configs on all 3 agents declare `auth: oauth` + `auth_url: https://mcp.linear.app/mcp` (user-owned `~/.brainchild/agents/` intentionally NOT modified — session 147 insulation promise). **Zero OAuth hangs at meeting join.** Known limitation: mcp-remote version upgrades create fresh cache dirs (users re-auth on bump); accepted for MVP.
- **15.7.4 (D) wizard credentials status screen + claude-code prereq check** (next, ~2h) — users enable freely, then see a per-MCP `✓/⚠/✗` checklist at the end of the MCP step with remediation URLs. Non-blocking. OAuth MCPs get an optional inline "authorize Linear now? y/n" that invokes the same code path as `brainchild auth <mcp>`. **Session 148 addition**: when user toggles `claude-code` on, probe `shutil.which("git")` + `shutil.which("claude")` + claude-is-authed check; skip if user says "later"; fails non-blockingly with the install-docs URL. Git-init is NOT a pre-req for enablement (per-call concern, MCP takes `repo_path` at invocation). Uses 15.7.1's `missing_vars` + 15.7.3's `_oauth_cache_exists`.
- **15.7.4.5 (E) runtime MCP pre-flight** (session 148 split-out, ~45m) — same `_report_mcp_readiness(mcp_servers)` helper runs in `_run_bot()` BEFORE browser spin-up. Missing OAuth → interactive "Run auth now? (y/N)" that invokes `brainchild auth <mcp>` inline, waits for token cache, continues. Missing env vars → "Continue without slack? (Y/n)". **Catches hand-edit-config case** (user enables OAuth MCP by editing yaml outside wizard — 15.7.3 banner catches it mid-meeting today but obtrusively). Wizard + runtime share the same helper; belt-and-suspenders. `--no-preflight` escape hatch for CI/scripted launches.

### New MCPs (15.7.5) and per-agent default enablement
**Rule (session 147):** an MCP is `enabled: true` on an agent **iff a bundled skill on that agent requires it.** Everything else is scaffolded but `enabled: false` — users surface them via the wizard. Prevents "enabled but silently unauthed" noise at meeting join.

Final matrix:
- **PM** → Linear ✓ (standup-summary optional use, ambient filing from spoken commitments) + Calendar ✓ (schedule-followup). GitHub dropped — no PM skill calls it.
- **Designer** → Figma ✓ (design-review-feedback + design-handoff-spec). Linear dropped — no Designer skill calls it.
- **Engineer** → GitHub ✓ (pr-review + release-notes) + Sentry ✓ (live-bug-triage) + claude-code ✓ (live-bug-triage delegate).
- **Slack, Salesforce, Playwright** → scaffolded in all three configs but `enabled: false` everywhere — no bundled skill paired. Users who want `post-recap-to-slack`, `deal-brief`, or `design-qa` flip them on in the wizard.
- Every new block declares `auth: env` + `credentials_url: "https://..."` — feeds 15.7.4's status screen.

**Behavior change on fresh installs:** PM and Designer lose a previously-enabled MCP each. `~/.brainchild/agents/` is user-owned per 14.3, so existing installs are insulated; only new installs (or `rm -rf ~/.brainchild/agents/` reseeds) see the narrower defaults. Acceptable for MVP — users who customized the defaults aren't surprised, and fresh installs have a quieter out-of-box experience.

### Skills (15.7.6)
Six new `SKILL.md` files, each following the existing `prd-from-discussion` / `design-review-feedback` pattern (frontmatter + `## Shape` + `## Rules` sections). `live-bug-triage` is the most complex — it chains Sentry MCP + Claude Code delegate. Others are single-MCP or pure-reasoning (`scope-estimate` writes no code, makes no tool calls).

### Estimation and launch impact
- **Total ~9–11h.** Session 148 shipped 15.7.1 + 15.7.2 + 15.7.3 in ~5h (three commits). Remaining: 15.7.4 ~2h (was 1.5h; claude-code prereq check added scope), 15.7.4.5 ~45m (new session-148 split-out), 15.7.5 2–3h, 15.7.6 2–3h. **Remaining envelope: ~6–8h.**
- MVP budget: 17.5h → 28–30h. Launch slips ~2 days from Apr 25–26 to Apr 28–30 aspirational.
- Deliberate bet: shipping a hardened MCP path + complete team-arc is worth 2 calendar days. Skill showcase during `brainchild setup` is the moment a user decides whether this product reads their mind.

### Open design questions (carry into execution)
1. **Non-mcp-remote OAuth paths** — the cache-check scheme in 15.7.3 is specific to `mcp-remote`'s directory layout (`~/.mcp-auth/mcp-remote-<version>/<md5(url)>_tokens.json`). If any future MCP ships its own OAuth flow outside `mcp-remote`, the readiness check needs a per-server convention (e.g., a callable `is_authorized()` hook declared in config). For v1 the five new MCPs are all API-key-based so this defers — Linear is still the only `mcp-remote` OAuth MCP in the roster.
2. **Salesforce + Playwright as "power-ups without bundled skills"** — intentional per session 147. Salesforce's likely v1.1 skill is `deal-brief` (pre-call account prep for PM); Playwright's likely v1.1 skill is `design-qa` (Designer; screenshot deployed URL + diff vs Figma frame). Neither blocks MVP — ship the MCP scaffolding now so users can wire them up + write their own skills, and the wizard surfaces them as discoverable options.

---

## Open Questions

1. **Wake phrase customization (voice)** — allow users to set their own wake phrase? Test Whisper reliability on custom phrases first. Chat wake phrase is already configurable via `chat_wake_phrase` in config.yaml.
2. **Linux distro coverage** — Ubuntu/Debian tier-1; PipeWire (Fedora, Ubuntu 22.04+) needs validation.

---

## Hard Won Knowledge

*Append-only log of bugs that were hard to diagnose. Each entry: what the bug was, what made it tricky, how it was fixed.*

- **`yaml.safe_dump` silently eats comments, blank lines, and hand-formatting.** (Session 121.) The setup wizard's edit-in-place mode runs `yaml.safe_load(existing_cfg)` → user edits → `yaml.safe_dump(cfg)` → writes back. Comments, section dividers, inline explanatory notes, and custom quoting all vanish. Surfaced when the user smoke-tested the wizard on `agents/{pm,designer,engineer}/config.yaml` — `git status` showed huge diffs even on presets that didn't change any wizard inputs, just because `yaml.safe_dump` round-trips drop everything the parser doesn't care about. What made it tricky: the wizard behaves correctly (values round-trip intact) so no test would catch it; you only see the damage in `git diff`. Mitigation for now: restored configs via `git checkout --`. Proper fix (deferred): swap to `ruamel.yaml` with `YAML(typ='rt')` — round-trip loader preserves comments and formatting. Or, only rewrite the specific fields the wizard touches (`enabled` flags, `skills.paths`) via a targeted string/diff approach. Not blocking; worth addressing before inviting external contributors who'll keep editing their configs by hand.
- **Rich markup parser swallows `[x]` in printed text.** (Session 119.) First draft of the power-ups toggle rendered checked items as `[x]` and unchecked as `[ ]`. `[ ]` printed literally (invalid markup), but `[x]` vanished entirely — Rich interpreted it as a (non-existent) style tag and stripped it. Took a minute to spot because the asymmetry only appeared when some items were default-checked. Fix: switched to `[✓]` (non-ASCII bracketed content isn't parsed as a style tag). Generalizable lesson: any `[letter]` or `[word]` in Rich-printed strings is at risk of being treated as markup — either escape with `\[` or use unicode glyphs.
- **Rich `Live` can't host `Prompt.ask`/`input()` mid-render.** (Session 121.) First attempt at step 3's "add your own skills" UX tried to pop a text input when a sentinel row was toggled mid-picker. Doesn't work — the `Live` region owns the terminal until exited, and input prompts don't compose with it. Fix: either exit the Live first (picker confirms → then prompt), or render a "queued action" hint and act on it after the picker closes. Final design landed on the former — `Confirm.ask` after the picker closes, path-input loop if confirmed.
- **Right-pane column squeezes inline sublabels past terminal-width truncation.** (Session 121.) Picker rows rendered `label <spaces> sublabel` on one line in a `Table.grid` left column; a 40-col build card in the right column left only ~32 cols for the left, and Rich silently truncated the dim sublabel text with no ellipsis. Looked like a 60-char cap bug at first because the skill subtitle *also* had a `desc[:60]` truncation in the code, which was a red herring — removing the slice didn't fix the visible cut-off. Fix: move sublabels to their own indented line under the label. No more horizontal-width race.
- **Rich `Panel.border_style` is a single value — no per-char frame colors.** (Session 122.) User asked for a rainbow frame on the build card. `Panel` accepts one `border_style` and applies it uniformly; there's no hook to vary color per character. Fix: drop `Panel` entirely and hand-compose the frame. Build top/bottom/side chars as raw strings, wrap each character with a fresh ANSI color + reset, join into a single string, and feed to `rich.text.Text.from_ansi` so Rich re-parses the sequences into styled segments at render time. Worth knowing because the obvious "style the Panel border" path is a dead end for any gradient/rainbow/per-char frame effect.
- **`len()` lies about cell width for wide glyphs (⚡, emoji).** (Session 122.) When hand-composing the rainbow card, naive `len(line)` padding misaligned the power-ups row because `⚡` is 2 terminal cells wide, not 1. Fix: `from rich.cells import cell_len` (or use `wcwidth`) for cell-accurate padding. Lesson applies any time you hand-compose ANSI-framed output instead of letting Rich's layout engine handle spacing.
- **`rich.prompt.Prompt.ask(..., default="")` renders an empty `()` in the label.** (Session 122.) The prompt text showed as `tagline (one line, under ~60 chars) ():` — Rich always appends `(default_value)` to the label when a default is set, and an empty-string default renders as an empty pair of parens. Fix: pass `show_default=False`. Non-obvious because the default value *itself* is correct and everything works — it's just cosmetic noise in the label.
- **`claude -p` in a non-interactive subprocess defaults to permission mode `ask` — which denies every Write/Edit/Bash.** (Session 125.) `delegate_to_claude_code` MCP spawns `claude -p <task> --worktree` as a stdio subprocess. In TTY-less contexts `ask` mode has no human to confirm with and auto-denies, so every file edit inside the worktree silently fails — the subprocess exits "success" but the tool list is effectively read-only. Surfaced only once we test-drove the harness: Engineer kept reporting "I wasn't able to write that file" for trivially-writable tasks. Fix: pass `--permission-mode bypassPermissions` explicitly (safe because Brainchild already confirm-gates each delegate call and `--worktree` throwaway-isolates the fs). Made the mode configurable via `DELEGATE_PERMISSION_MODE` env var in `agents/engineer/config.yaml → mcp_servers.delegate.env` so users who want a tighter sandbox can pick `acceptEdits` (file ops yes, Bash no). Lesson: whenever an LLM CLI is spawned as a subprocess and behaves like it has fewer tools than expected, check the permission mode first — it's almost always the culprit and the symptom (silent no-op) looks like anything but a permission issue.
- **LLM routes local-path questions to GitHub MCP when it has both `github__*` and `delegate` tools available.** (Session 125.) Engineer's first harness session: asked "how many python files are in pipeline/?", model called `github__search_code(query='path:pipeline/ extension:py', repo='<guessed>/<guessed>')` — hit 404s, didn't recover. It has no way to know "this path is local not remote" from tool schemas alone; github's description sounds plausible for any repo-ish question. Fix: add an explicit tool-routing paragraph to the bot's `llm.system_prompt`: `github__*` is for *remote* repos the user names by owner/repo; any local path = delegate to Claude Code; "when in doubt, prefer delegate." Generalizable: whenever two tools have overlapping surface area (both can "read code"), you need a routing rule in the prompt — tool descriptions alone aren't enough signal.
- **`ChatRunner` treats `connector._connected = False` as an unexpected disconnect.** (Session 125.) First `TerminalConnector` draft implemented `/quit` by flipping `_connected` to `False` — clean stop, right? But `ChatRunner._loop` calls `connector.is_connected()` every tick and on `False` prints "Meeting connection lost" plus the reconnection-attempt warnings from the Meet disconnect path. Visible as noise on the user's final `/quit`. Fix: route stdin `/quit`/EOF through `os.kill(os.getpid(), signal.SIGINT)` to trigger the existing SIGINT handler cleanly — same exit path as Ctrl-C. Generalizable: any new connector should distinguish "user asked to leave" (signal) from "connection died" (flag). Only the second one is a `_connected = False`.
- **`claude -p --resume <id>` looks up sessions by cwd, and must NOT be combined with `--worktree`.** (Session 126.) Setting up per-repo continuity in the delegate MCP meant pairing `--worktree` on first call with `--resume` on follow-ups. Two non-obvious traps: (a) running `claude -p ... --resume <id>` from the *parent repo* cwd errors with `No conversation found with session ID: <id>` — the session registry is indexed by project dir, and `--worktree` on first call changed the project dir to the worktree, so resume only works when cwd = the worktree path; (b) passing both `--resume` and `--worktree` on the same invocation does NOT reuse the original sandbox — `--worktree` spawns a brand-new one. Compounding: `claude --resume` with a bad session id exits 0 and writes the error to *stdout* as plain text, not JSON — so our JSON parser has to treat non-JSON stdout as an error path (not just stderr or non-zero exit). Fix: on resume, `cwd=worktree_path`, command has `--resume <id>` only, no `--worktree`. And on any non-JSON stdout containing "No conversation found", fall back to spawning a fresh `--worktree` call (handles the case where the user manually deleted the worktree dir between calls). Surfaced during verification in `/tmp/delegate_verify/` before committing the rewrite — first resume attempt from the parent repo failed silently from the MCP's POV (empty result), only the raw `claude` CLI run showed the "No conversation found" line.
- **`git diff` ignores untracked files by default — `land_worktree_changes` needs `git add -A` first.** (Session 126.) Claude Code's subprocess consistently leaves new files it creates **untracked** in the worktree (it only commits on explicit request). `land_worktree_changes` was computing `git -C <worktree> diff <base_sha>` to produce a patch for `git apply`, and the diff was empty even when the sandbox clearly had new files — because `git diff` (without `--cached` or `HEAD`) compares the working-tree version of *tracked* files against the index, and untracked files aren't in either. First landing attempt returned "No changes to land" for a sandbox containing an untracked `marker.txt` with content. Fix: `git -C <worktree> add -A` before the diff, then `git diff --cached <base_sha>` — staging pulls untracked files into the index so they appear in the diff. Side-effect-free because worktrees are throwaway sandboxes; staging them doesn't affect the parent repo's index or anywhere the user would notice.
- **Terminal harness pins `get_participant_count()` to 2 to force 1-on-1 mode.** (Session 125.) `ChatRunner` requires the `@brainchild` trigger phrase in rooms with >`ONE_ON_ONE_THRESHOLD` (=2) participants. A terminal session has one human and one bot — conceptually 2 participants. Returning 1 would trip the alone-exit grace timer. Returning anything ≥3 would force the user to type `@brainchild` before every message, breaking the test-drive UX. Pinning to exactly 2 is the sweet spot. Worth capturing because it's a non-obvious coupling between a "test harness" and the meeting-mode logic — future connectors (Slack? Discord? CLI chat?) all face the same decision.
- **MagicMock falls through `or` as truthy — mock the method or the `or` default never fires.** (Session 129.) Added `MCPClient.tool_timeout_for(tool_name)` and wired `chat_runner` to read it as `self._mcp.tool_timeout_for(tc["name"]) or config.TOOL_TIMEOUT_SECONDS`. Unit tests started failing with `TypeError: '<=' not supported between instances of 'MagicMock' and 'int'`. Cause: test mocks built via `MagicMock()` auto-create the new method as another MagicMock, which is **truthy**, so `or` short-circuits on it and returns the mock itself — which then fails integer comparison downstream in the heartbeat/timeout math. Fix: explicit `mcp.tool_timeout_for.return_value = None` in every fixture that builds a MagicMock'd MCP. Generalizable: any time you add a new method to an interface that's MagicMock'd in tests, every existing fixture needs an explicit stub for that method — MagicMock's "just works" default behavior is exactly what trips `or`/`and`/truthy-check fallbacks.
- **`idle_timeout_seconds` wasn't what it sounded like.** (Session 129.) Config had an `idle_timeout_seconds: 600` under `connector:` on every bot. Name implied "how long Brainchild waits in an idle browser before giving up." grep showed the constant was actually the max wait for the user to admit the bot from the Meet lobby (`connectors/macos_adapter.py:354` — a polling loop during the knock/admit phase). Two wrongs compound: the name doesn't describe the behavior, and power users adjust it to cover a different scenario than the one it controls. Fix: renamed to `LOBBY_WAIT_SECONDS` in `config.py`, updated both connector callsites. Lesson: any config key still wearing a name from an earlier architecture is tech debt — grep its reads when auditing, don't trust the name.
- **`git commit` without `-a` silently drops unstaged edits after `git mv`.** (Session 143.) The templates → agents collapse did four things: `git mv src/brainchild/templates/agents src/brainchild/agents` (17 renames auto-staged by git), Edit the two `_TEMPLATES_DIR` → `_BUNDLED_AGENTS_DIR` Python references, Edit `pyproject.toml` comment, Edit `docs/roadmap.md` row. Ran `git commit -m ...` — commit landed as "17 files changed, 0 insertions, 0 deletions" (all renames), and the 4 Edit-tool changes were left dangling in the working tree, unstaged. What made it tricky: every verification step passed. Tests ran against the working tree (where edits were applied), wheel built correctly (same), install round-trip worked (same). Only caught because a post-commit `git status --short` still showed 4 dirty files. The broken commit `3d8582a` in isolation would import-error on first run — the directory was renamed but `_TEMPLATES_DIR = .../templates/agents` still pointed at the old path. Fix: follow-up commit `3e4f23e` bundled the dangling edits with a message explaining the atomic intent belonged with `3d8582a`. Not amended per user's append-only history preference. Lesson: when a commit mixes `git mv` (auto-staged) with file edits from other tools, always run `git status --short` before `git commit` to see what's staged vs modified — or use `git commit -a` to capture tracked-file modifications. "Tests pass" is not sufficient signal because tests run against the working tree, not the staged index.
- **`pipdeptree --reverse` silently omits parents that use extras.** (Session 144.) Dep audit: `pipdeptree --reverse --packages cryptography` in a clean install of the 7 pinned direct deps returned "no reverse dependents" even though `cryptography==46.0.7` was clearly installed. Initially looked like pip had installed an orphan. Root cause: `mcp==1.27.0` declares `pyjwt[crypto]>=2.10.1`, and the `[crypto]` extra pulls `cryptography>=3.4.0`. Extras-based parent links live in the package's `requires_dist` metadata with an `extra == "crypto"` marker, not in the flat `Requires:` field `pipdeptree` reads. The tool had no way to see the edge, so it presented cryptography as rootless. What made it tricky: the symptom ("nothing requires this, yet it's installed") is the same symptom a truly phantom dep would produce — so it's easy to mistake a real transitive for a phantom and drop it. Fix/method: use `pip install --dry-run --report <file>.json` instead — the JSON report includes every resolved package's full `requires_dist` list, including `extra == "..."` markers, so the real parent chain becomes visible. Generalizable rule: whenever `pipdeptree --reverse` says "no parent" for something pip clearly chose to install, don't believe it — re-verify via the install report before declaring a dep phantom. Confirmed phantom in this session: `requests` (absent from the resolved tree, floor dropped). Confirmed real via the report: `cryptography`.
- **`~/.brainchild/agents/` shadows the bundled template after first run — bundle edits go stale until you nuke the user dir.** (Session 146.) Did a `delegate → claude-code` yaml-key rename across all three bundled configs in `src/brainchild/agents/`, confirmed by file inspection + test suite. But `BRAINCHILD_BOT=engineer python -c "from brainchild import config; print(list(config.MCP_SERVERS.keys()))"` still returned `['delegate', 'github']` after every re-import. Not a caching issue — `config.py` reads `~/.brainchild/agents/<name>/config.yaml`, and the user-level copy had been written on an earlier `brainchild` run via the first-run auto-copy hook (session-142 behavior, seed-once-then-own). After that first copy, the user dir is the source of truth; the bundled template is just a seed for fresh installs. What made it tricky: the bundle was clearly correct, tests (which read the src-layout path directly) passed, but runtime looked completely unaffected by the rename. User asked to `rm -rf ~/.brainchild/agents/`, next `brainchild` invocation re-ran the auto-copy from the updated bundle, MCPs loaded as `['claude-code', 'github']` on the first try. Generalizable: any time a bundle edit "doesn't take" at runtime, check `~/.brainchild/agents/` — the user-level copies are almost certainly shadowing it. Dev-loop rule for template edits: `rm -rf ~/.brainchild/agents/` after the edit, OR point `_AGENTS_DIR` at a temp directory in tests that need to exercise the auto-copy path. Also a real UX concern for users: they'll hit the same thing if they pull a new Brainchild version that changes a bundled config, because the update won't reach their user dir without an explicit refresh.
- **String-literal CLI-surface audits miss positional-argv test shapes.** (Session 150.) The 15.8.0 audit of the bare `brainchild <name>` form grepped for literal strings like `brainchild pm` / `brainchild {name}` / `brainchild <name>` across the tree and declared `tests/test_entry_cli.py` a zero-hit category because no assertion message contains that phrase. Wrong: `test_main_known_bot_dispatches_to_run_bot` and `test_main_unknown_bot_returns_2` both exercised the bare form as `patched_argv(["pm", "<url>"])` and `patched_argv(["ghost"])` — positional argv lists no string-literal grep catches. What made it tricky: the files *were* in the audit scope and skimmed, but the eye scans for string matches of the rename pattern, not for argv-list shapes whose semantics depend on the dispatcher. Fix was mechanical (rename + add 3 tests for the new dispatcher branches). Lesson: when auditing a CLI surface for rename, every test file that exercises `main()` or the dispatcher needs a semantic read (what shape of argv does this pass? what dispatch branch does it cover?) not just a string-match pass. Better audit prompt: "find every place that invokes the CLI — strings OR argv-structured."
- **Claude Code's real MCP list lives in `claude mcp list`, not `~/.claude.json#mcpServers`.** (Session 151.) Initial design for the `claude` bundled agent's auto-import assumed user MCPs would be in `~/.claude.json#mcpServers` — the canonical Claude Code settings file. Wrote the JSON-parse path first, unit-tested it, then ran it against the author's real home and got **zero MCPs** despite the user obviously having Gmail + Drive + Calendar + Linear connected. Dug into `~/.claude.json` and found the `mcpServers` key literally empty; the 4 active MCPs lived only in `claude mcp list` output because they're claude.ai *account-level* connectors (configured in the claude.ai UI, not in any local JSON). Projects section had `enabledMcpjsonServers` referencing project-scoped MCPs but nothing at the user level. What made it tricky: the JSON path worked correctly and tested cleanly — the bug was "tested against the wrong source of truth." Fix: added a second discovery path that shells out to `claude mcp list` and regex-parses the text output (10s timeout, non-match skip, degrades to empty on format drift). Hosted URLs auto-wrap via `mcp-remote@0.1.38`. Lesson: when integrating with another tool's config, don't assume the config file is the source of truth — many modern CLIs have hybrid local-file + account-backend state, and the *authoritative* list is whatever the tool itself reports when you ask it. Always verify against a real user's setup before freezing the API shape. Fragility risk: if Claude Code ever changes the `claude mcp list` output format, imports silently return zero — Phase 17 upstream-drift watch should monitor `_CLAUDE_MCP_LIST_RE` in `pipeline/claude_code_import.py`.
- **OAuth-over-mcp-remote surfaces no sniffable error on missing/cancelled auth.** (Session 148.) Empirical probe in 15.7.1a: boot `npx -y mcp-remote https://mcp.linear.app/sse` with an empty cache dir, call a tool. Browser pops open with OAuth URL; stdio `session.initialize()` stalls indefinitely until our explicit 45s timeout fires with a `TimeoutError`. User clicking **Cancel** on the Linear popup produces the same stall — no "auth denied" error travels back through the MCP channel. What made it important: the whole 15.7.1d sniff list was originally conceived to handle Linear-style auth failures, but Linear has no string to sniff. Reshaped scope: runtime sniff covers API-key MCPs only; OAuth MCPs are detected proactively via 15.7.3 cache-path check. Generalizable: whenever a pre-meeting auth check is being designed, assume any `mcp-remote`-backed server can only be detected by looking at its token cache on disk, not by interpreting runtime errors.
- **Renaming beats retyping when changing a dict's value shape.** (Session 148.) 15.7.1 had to upgrade `MCPClient.failed_servers: dict[str, str]` to `dict[str, dict]`. Python won't flag a type change — code like `for name, reason in failed_servers.items(): log.error(reason)` keeps running but prints `{'kind': ..., 'vars': [...]}` as a stringified dict into the log. Chose to rename to `startup_failures` (and `disabled_servers` → `runtime_failures`) instead. Every stale consumer now raises `AttributeError` on first access — `__main__.py`, `chat_runner.py`, and two test files all surfaced immediately at test time and got updated in one pass. No "found a stringified dict in logs three weeks later" surprise. Generalizable: dynamic-typed languages hide shape changes; when you can't rely on the type checker, use the name as a tripwire.
- **mcp-remote's token cache key = `md5(auth_url)` where `auth_url` is the URL mcp-remote hashes internally — which may differ from the positional arg.** (Session 148.) Confirmed by reading `dist/chunk-*.js` at `~/.npm/_npx/.../mcp-remote/`: `getServerUrlHash(serverUrl, authorizeResource, headers)` returns `md5([serverUrl, authorizeResource?, headers?].join("|"))`. For the no-headers/no-authorize_resource happy path (every server we ship), it's just `md5(serverUrl)`. Subtle catch verified against local disk: the existing tokens file is `~/.mcp-auth/mcp-remote-0.1.37/fcc436b0d1e0a1ed9a2b15bbd638eb13_tokens.json`, which is `md5("https://mcp.linear.app/mcp")` — **not** `md5` of the `/sse` URL the config passes as the positional arg. The probe lockfile (session-scoped) matches the `/sse` hash, but the tokens cache uses `/mcp`. Best guess: http-first transport strategy normalizes to `/mcp` internally before caching. For the check to work reliably, the bundled config needs an explicit `auth_url` field that the bundle author declares, not derived from args. Two other gotchas while implementing: (a) version dir (`mcp-remote-0.1.37`) bumps on package upgrade so cache is per-version — locally-upgraded mcp-remote creates a fresh dir and effectively forces re-auth until the user reruns `brainchild auth linear`; (b) existence ≠ validity — a revoked or refresh-failed token still has a file on disk, so the check is "will mcp-remote hang at boot waiting for browser OAuth" not "will the next tool call succeed." Runtime 401 sniff (15.7.1d) handles the second half orthogonally for API-key MCPs; for OAuth MCPs it's still a runtime surprise if the refresh token has expired.
- **MCP spec has no semantic error taxonomy — every host does substring sniffing.** (Session 148.) The JSON-RPC substrate has standardized protocol-level errors (parse error, method not found, invalid params), but application-level failure shapes are entirely server-author-defined. `isError: true` tool results ship as free-form text (GitHub "Bad credentials", Figma "Forbidden", Slack "invalid_auth", Sentry "Invalid token", Google gRPC "UNAUTHENTICATED", etc.) with no machine-readable `error_code` field. Every MCP host in the ecosystem (Claude Desktop, Cursor, Continue) runs substring sniffing for auth-like patterns — it's the state of the art, not a workaround. Implication for future bundle additions: whenever adding a new MCP, re-run `tests/probe_auth_errors.py` against it with a bogus credential and append captured strings to `docs/mcp-auth-errors.md` + `_AUTH_ERROR_PATTERNS`. Accept that false negatives ship downgraded UX (LLM relays verbatim instead of banner showing "re-auth"), not silent failure.
- **Bundled MCP `command`/`args` that are relative paths break silently the moment CWD assumptions shift.** (Session 154.) The `claude` agent's `claude-code` MCP had `command: python, args: ["agents/engineer/claude_code.py"]` — worked for a year because the launcher `cd`'s to REPO_DIR before dispatch, so the relative path resolved against the repo root. Post-src-layout packaging the file moved to `src/brainchild/agents/engineer/claude_code.py`; the relative path no longer matched; MCP subprocess died with `[Errno 2] No such file or directory` at spawn. Same class of bug had been sitting in all four bundled agents as `command: "./github-mcp-server"` for a separate Go binary — dormant today because it was only `enabled: true` on engineer and the launcher's `cd` was masking it. Both bugs would detonate under `uv tool install` (Phase 14.5) because the installed CLI's CWD is the user's invocation dir, not any reliable repo root. What made it tricky: no existing test exercised bundled configs end-to-end. `test_mcp_client.py` spawned a *synthetic* test server at an absolute tmp path; `test_config_loader.py` validated YAML→dict parsing with *synthetic* YAML; neither one loaded `src/brainchild/agents/*/config.yaml`. Fixes applied: `args: ["-m", "brainchild.agents.engineer.claude_code"]` for the python script (namespace-package import works without `__init__.py` under PEP 420; CWD-independent in dev and installed); `command: "github-mcp-server"` (bare name, PATH lookup) for the Go binary. Prevention landed in the same session as `tests/test_bundled_mcps_bootable_static.py` — walks every bundled config, every MCP block (enabled AND disabled, since shipping the definition implies boot must work), and asserts `command`+`args` resolve via one of: `shutil.which` for bare names, `importlib.util.find_spec` for `-m <mod>`, absolute-path-exists for `python <script>`, executable-check for absolute commands. Relative paths fail with a pointed message naming `uv tool install` as the reason. Generalizable lesson: any bundled config entry that's a filesystem path has to be either (a) an absolute path resolvable via the package (`Path(brainchild.__file__).parent / "..."`), (b) a module-path invocation, or (c) a bare name on PATH. Everything else is latent rot. And the test suite has to exercise the *actual* bundled configs — synthetic YAML and synthetic MCP servers won't catch shipping-contract drift.
- **Wizard-time modules can't `from brainchild import config` — config.py asserts `BRAINCHILD_BOT` at import.** (Session 159.) First run of the new Phase 14.10 wizard step died at `brainchild setup` with `ERROR: BRAINCHILD_BOT env var is not set.` — not a runtime check, the assertion fired on `from brainchild.pipeline.setup import run` because `setup.py` now imports `google_signin.py`, which had `from brainchild import config` at module top, which trips line 13 of `config.py` before the wizard even starts. The wizard's whole purpose is to choose a bot, so by definition `BRAINCHILD_BOT` is unset when it runs. Pattern was already documented in `setup.py`'s comment around `_ENV_FILE`: "Inlined rather than imported from brainchild.config because config.py triggers a BRAINCHILD_BOT gate at import time and the wizard runs before a bot is chosen." Fix: same compromise — inline the three path constants (`_BROWSER_PROFILE_DIR`, `_AUTH_STATE_FILE`, `_GOOGLE_ACCOUNT_FILE`) in `google_signin.py`, plus a private `_auth_state_has_sid()` helper that mirrors `connectors.session.validate_auth_state` without the import chain (validate_auth_state itself is fine to call at runtime since session.py only imports config lazily under `save_debug`, but importing it still drags `from brainchild import config` at session.py's module top). Three-way regression guard added (`test_google_signin_paths_canonical_across_modules`) to fail loud if anyone updates `config.GOOGLE_ACCOUNT_FILE` without lockstep-updating `google_signin._GOOGLE_ACCOUNT_FILE`. Lesson: any module imported during wizard execution (anything reachable from `_run_setup`'s import graph) is bound by the same constraint — must not transitively import config. When adding pre-bot-selection wizard code, run `BRAINCHILD_BOT= python -c "..."` to verify the import chain is clean before live-testing.
- **Playwright bundled "Chrome for Testing" can't open profiles created by real `Google Chrome.app` — process dies on launch with no useful error.** (Session 159.) New `_launch_signin_flow` opened `~/.brainchild/browser_profile/` via `p.chromium.launch_persistent_context(user_data_dir=...)` without setting `executable_path`. Default Playwright path is the bundled `Google Chrome for Testing` binary (`~/Library/Caches/ms-playwright/chromium-1208/chrome-mac-arm64/...`). The user's `browser_profile/` was created by real `Google Chrome.app` per `macos_adapter.py:512` (`executable_path="/Applications/Google Chrome.app/Contents/MacOS/Google Chrome"`). Chrome refuses to open profiles across binary versions/distributions — launched process exited immediately with `kill EPERM` and the Playwright API surfaced `BrowserType.launch_persistent_context: Target page, context or browser has been closed`. The actual cause was visible only in the verbose browser-logs dump as a cryptic `<gracefully close start>` followed by `<process did exit: exitCode=null, signal=SIGTRAP>` — the SIGTRAP comes from Chrome's own profile-version mismatch protection. Fix: pass `executable_path="/Applications/Google Chrome.app/Contents/MacOS/Google Chrome"` to match the adapter exactly, so the wizard seeds a profile the runtime adapter can read and vice versa. Generalizable: when any Playwright path touches the persistent profile, the binary identity must be the same one the runtime uses — there's no portability across Chrome distributions. (Cross-platform implication: a future Linux adapter that uses `chromium` as the persistent-profile binary will need its own `executable_path` resolution; bundled Chrome-for-Testing might be acceptable on Linux but the choice has to be locked once and matched everywhere.)
- **Rich `Prompt.ask` with `[letter]` markup eats brackets even in label text.** (Session 159.) Same trap as session 119's `[x]` bug, recurred in a different shape. Initial detect-branch prompt was `Prompt.ask("[enter] continue with this account · [r] sign in with a different account", choices=["", "r"], default="")`. Rendered as garbled `" continue with this account ·  sign in with a different account"` — Rich parsed `[enter]` and `[r]` as nonexistent style tags and stripped them. User couldn't tell what to type. Fix: reframed as conventional yes/no on the *non-default* path: `Prompt.ask("Sign in with a different account?", choices=["y", "n"], default="n")`. Cleaner UX too — matches git/brew/apt convention, default = continue with current, capitalized N in the rendered `[y/n] (n)` cues the safe choice. Generalizable: any time you find yourself writing `[word]` or `[letter]` inside Rich text, either escape with `\[`, use unicode brackets like `「」` or parentheses, or — better — refactor to a yes/no with `choices=...` so Rich renders the affordance for you. Don't fight Rich's markup parser, work with its prompt API.
- **Rich `Panel(width=N)` is NOT an absolute width — it caps, not locks, unless `expand=True`.** (Session 153.) User reported the build card "expanding and contracting with each selection" during the setup wizard. First reading of the code looked correct: `Panel(inner, width=40, padding=(0,0))`. But Rich's default `expand=True` makes the panel fill available width in its container *up to* `width=`; with `expand=False`, the panel *shrinks to fit content* up to `width=`. Neither is "always exactly N cells." Rich models width as a ceiling, not a fixed value. So when the wizard's `Table.grid` left column was narrow (short "custom" tagline) the panel hit the ceiling from above and stretched to 40; when it was wide (long preset tagline) the panel could have stretched further but the cap held it at 40; and short-content renders with `expand=False` shrank the panel to content-length. User read this as "expanding and contracting" because subjectively the card *did* change size between renders. What made it tricky: naïve fix was `expand=False` — which actually made it worse because now the "custom" card rendered narrower than preset cards (shrink-to-content). The right fix is `expand=True` + `width=N` together: expand fills up to the ceiling, ceiling is explicit, result is truly fixed. Also discovered downstream: `Panel(width=40)` inside a `Table.grid` cell can still get clipped on narrow terminals if `left_col_min + padding + 40 > console.size.width` — Rich has to cut something and chooses the panel's right border/content. Fix there was terminal-aware sizing (`build_card.width_for(console)` clamps between `MIN_WIDTH=28` and `DEFAULT_WIDTH=40` based on `console.size.width - 34`). Generalizable: whenever a Rich layout needs a truly fixed dimension, always pair `width=N` with `expand=True` AND ensure the parent layout has enough room — the "just set width" intuition from CSS/Tk doesn't transfer. Also: every Rich component that takes `width` should be re-checked for `expand` semantics when the layout evolves, because `expand`'s default varies by component.
- **Bundled-vs-user config drift silently ignores your edits — `_ensure_user_agents` only seeds missing bots, never updates.** (Session 156.) User flipped `captions_enabled: true` in the *bundled* `src/brainchild/agents/claude/config.yaml`, restarted the bot, and found the caption pipeline still dark in `/tmp/brainchild.log` (no `caption bridge exposed`, no `caption: [...]`, no transcript wiring). The runtime copy at `~/.brainchild/agents/claude/config.yaml` still had `captions_enabled: false` — the runtime reads that file, not the bundled one. Root cause: `_ensure_user_agents` at `src/brainchild/__main__.py:95` uses `if not dest.exists(): shutil.copytree(bundled, dest)` — a per-bot, create-only seed. Deliberately additive so wizard edits and hand-tweaks are never stomped, but the cost is that *any* bundled-config edit post-first-install is invisible to existing installs. What made it tricky: the diagnosis was upside-down. Initial instinct was "check config.py's CAPTIONS_ENABLED wiring" or "maybe the caption observer failed to inject." The actual fix was "read the file the runtime actually loads, not the one in your editor." The log silence was the key signal — had the caption pipeline wired and failed at the JS-bridge or MutationObserver layer, there would have been log lines from `MacOSAdapter: caption bridge exposed` or `captions: Shift+C failed`. Nothing from the caption subsystem at all meant nothing was wired, which meant `config.CAPTIONS_ENABLED` was `False` at import time, which meant the on-disk file had `false` regardless of what was in the editor. Compounding: the bundled config's header comment said "Captions off by default — Claude's value is chat-directed delegation, not ambient transcript parsing" while the value itself was `true` (dev-time flip, comment left stale). So even if you noticed the file the dev hat was on, the comment would tell you the intended default was `false`, reinforcing the wrong mental model. Fix: (a) edit the runtime copy for the session, (b) rewrite the bundled comment to match the `true` value, (c) add `brainchild edit <bot|.env>` and `brainchild where <bot|.env>` subcommands (commit `01b0868`) so users of any install shape can reach the runtime config in one command and never repeat this "I edited the wrong file" loop. Generalizable lesson: whenever a feature silently doesn't happen at runtime, the fastest debug path is "grep `/tmp/brainchild.log` for any log line from the subsystem" — presence vs absence of subsystem log lines discriminates "wiring missing" from "wiring failed" faster than reading the code does, and drift bugs between bundled and user config always present as the former. Open architectural gap: `brainchild setup --sync-bundled` would surface bundled-to-user drift with per-key accept/skip prompts; not yet built. Dev-mode symlink (`~/.brainchild/agents/<bot>` → `src/brainchild/agents/<bot>`) would let bundled edits hit runtime immediately during development; also not yet built.
- **Tool-confirmation prompts self-poisoned the LLM context when persisted as `kind="chat"`.** (Session 127.) `ChatRunner._request_confirmation` sends "I'd like to run X. OK?" into chat and `_send` appended it to the meeting record. On the next turn, `MeetingRecord.tail()` replayed it to the model as a prior assistant message — the model learned to mimic the harness's own wording as *plain text* before emitting a real `tool_call`. Symptoms: (a) the user saw two confirmation prompts per call (a hallucinated one from the model, then the real one from the harness) and had to type "ok" twice; (b) occasionally after the user's "ok", the model skipped the real tool_call and just hallucinated a result — caught during Phase 15.5.7 step 6 smoke when Engineer reported "README.md" as the contents of a repo that actually held `f.txt`. What made it tricky: no single line in the code was wrong — each piece (persist chat to record, replay tail to model, prompt for confirmation in chat) was correct in isolation; the bug was an emergent feedback loop from all three composing. Looked like a prompt-engineering problem at first (add a "don't parrot confirmations" nudge to system prompt) until reframed as "why are harness prompts in the LLM's prompt at all?". Fix: `_send` gained a `kind` kwarg; `_request_confirmation` passes `kind="confirmation"`; user replies while `_pending_tool_call` is set are also tagged `kind="confirmation"` in `_loop`. `pipeline/llm.py` already filtered `tail()` to `kind in {chat, caption}`, so one-word keyword change made the whole harness-plumbing layer invisible to the model while keeping the full audit trail in the JSONL. Generalizable: any text the harness *shows in chat for UX reasons* is not the same as a conversation turn — keep them in separate lanes from day one, or you'll get mimicry bugs that masquerade as model hallucinations.
